When the Cook's Wage Becomes Due: Custom and Feast Types
Ruling on when cooking wage is due based on custom and feast types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a cooking wage becomes due, explain the role of custom ('urf), and distinguish between the restricted and generalized views regarding feast types.

Core Idea
Wage for cooking is due after gharf (placing food in bowls), based on custom — custom governs where no text exists.

You have hired a cook to prepare a feast. When does he become entitled to his wage? The classical Hanafi text addresses this, ruling that the wage is due after the food is placed into serving bowls (gharf). This ruling is founded on custom ('urf), which is a recognized secondary source of law in the Hanafi school. However, there is a nuance: some scholars restrict this to wedding feasts (walimah), while others generalize it to any invitation feast. Understanding this requires you to grasp the weight of custom in Hanafi fiqh and the diversity of feast types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring a cook. The ruling is that the wage becomes wajib (obligatory for the employer to pay) after the cook has performed 'gharf' – placing the food into serving bowls. This is the point of completion according to custom.
Gharf is defined as transferring broth from pots to bowls, essentially plating the food.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof for this timing is custom ('urf). In the Hanafi school, custom is a legitimate source of law in matters where no explicit text (nass) from Quran or Sunnah exists. The principle is 'al-thābit bi al-'urf ka al-thābit bi al-sharṭ' (what is established by custom is like what is established by stipulation).
There is no direct Quranic or hadith text specifying when a cooking wage is due; hence custom fills the gap.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The specific element of custom is that people generally consider the cooking work complete once the food is plated. They do not wait for serving. This widespread practice, not contradicting any nass, becomes a valid determinant of rights.
Custom must be consistent and general (not isolated) to be legally binding.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute)
Al-Quduri and the author of al-Multaqa restrict this ruling to food prepared for a wedding feast (walimah). They argue that for family meals or other non-invitation feasts, there is no established custom. The author of the matn (Marghinani or similar) generalizes it to all types of feasts, listing ten varieties.
The commentator supports the generalization by citing many feast types and noting that 'walimah' can encompass all invitation food.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The commentator sides with the author's generalization, and this is likely the muftā bihī (operative ruling) because it is more comprehensive and accounts for diverse customs. The generalization aligns with the Hanafi reliance on custom without arbitrarily limiting it.
The list of feasts includes walimah (wedding), khurs (childbirth), aqiqah (shaving head), ighdar (circumcision), hanaqah (Quran completion), milaak (marriage), ma'dabah (invitation without cause), wakirah (building completion), naqi'ah (return from travel), wadiḥah (calamity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
11 قوله: وللطبخ الخ؛ أي وللمؤجر طلب الأجرة من المستأجر للطبخ بعد وضع الطعام في القصاع، اعتباراً للعرف، فإنَّ المعتبر هو العادة فيما لا نص فيه، والقُدوري وصاحب «الملتقى» (1) وغيرهما قيدوه بأن يكون الطعام للوليمة نظراً إلى أنه لو كان لأهل بيته فلا عرف عليه للعرف. وإنما أطلقه المصنف له نظراً إلى أن للأطعمة أنواعاً: الوليمة: وهو طعام العرس، والخرس: وهو طعام الولادة. والعقيقة: وهو عند حلق شعر المولود. والإغدار: وهو طعام الختان. والحناقة: وهو الطعام عند ختم الصبي حفظ القرآن. والملاك: وهو الطعام عند التزوج. والمأدبة: وهو طعام صنع الدعوة بلا سبب. والوكيرة: وهو الطعام عند فراغ البنيان. والنقيعة: وهو طعام القادم من سفره. والوضيحة: وهو طعام المصيبة. والعتيرة: شاة كانوا يذبحونها لآلهتهم، ونظمها بعض الفضلاء، وذكر هذا النظم العلامة الطحطاوي (2)، وغيره. والوليمة قد تعمّ كل طعام هيئ على طريق الدعوة، كما لا يخفى على من له نظر إلى المحاورات، ومن قيده بكون الطعام للوليمة نظر إلى هذا التعميم، والله عليم حكيم. [2] قوله: بعد الغرف؛ الغَرف بفتح الغين المعجمة وسكون الراء المهملة: إخراج المرق من القدور إلى القصاع ذكره في «المعدن» وغيره، وحاصله: جعل الطعام في القصعة، وفيه إيماء إلى أنّ تسوية الخوان ووضع القصاع واجب على الطباخ كما قيل
His saying: 'And for cooking after the gharf' meaning the hirer can demand the wage from the customer for cooking after placing the food in bowls, based on custom (urf), for what is considered is the custom in matters where there is no text. Al-Quduri and the author of al-Multaqa and others restricted it to food for a wedding feast (walimah), because if it were for his family, there is no custom concerning it. The author gave it absolutely considering that foods have types: Walimah: wedding food. Khurs: food for childbirth. Aqiqah: at the shaving of the newborn's hair. Ighdar: circumcision food. Hanaqah: food when a child completes Quran memorization. Milaak: food at marriage. Ma'dabah: food made for invitation without cause. Wakirah: food upon completion of building. Naqi'ah: food for a traveler returning. Wadiḥah: food for calamity. Atirah: a sheep they used to slaughter for their gods. Some scholars versified these, and Allamah al-Tahawi mentioned this versification. Walimah may encompass all food prepared by way of invitation, as is clear to those familiar with usage. The one who restricted it to wedding food looked to this generalization. And Allah is All-Knowing, Wise. [2] His saying: 'after the gharf'; gharf (with fathah on ghayn and sukoon on ra') means taking broth from pots into bowls, mentioned in al-Ma'dan and others. Its essence is placing food in the bowl. This indicates that laying the table and placing bowls is obligatory on the cook, as is said.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on when a cook is entitled to his wage. The base matn states that the wage for cooking is due 'after the gharf', meaning after the food is placed into serving bowls. The commentator explains that this is based on custom (urf), which is the legitimate source of law in matters where no explicit text (nass) exists. Al-Quduri and others restrict this ruling to food prepared for a wedding feast (walimah), because for family meals, there is no established custom about when the wage is due. However, the author of this book (presumably the matn author) gives an absolute ruling, considering the various types of feast foods that exist. The commentator then lists ten types of feasts: walimah (wedding), khurs (childbirth), aqiqah (shaving head), ighdar (circumcision), hanaqah (completion of Quran), milaak (marriage), ma'dabah (invitation without reason), wakirah (completion of building), naqi'ah (return from travel), and wadiḥah (calamity). He also mentions atirah (pre-Islamic sacrifice). He notes that walimah can be generalized to any food prepared for an invitation. The term 'gharf' is defined as taking broth from pots into bowls, implying that the cook is also responsible for arranging the table and placing bowls, which is considered part of his duties.

Key Terms
الغرف (gharf): The act of transferring food (especially broth) from cooking pots into serving bowls; the point at which the cooking wage becomes due.
الوليمة (walimah): In this context, food prepared for a wedding feast, but also can refer to any food prepared for an invitation.
العرف (urf): Customary practice that is considered a valid source of law in matters not regulated by explicit texts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does a cook become entitled to his wage for cooking?
A) Immediately when he starts cooking
B) After the food is placed into serving bowls (gharf)
C) Only after the guests have eaten
D) After the food is fully cooked but not yet served

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes the timing of a cooking wage by custom ('urf), which is a valid legal source in the absence of explicit texts, and the wage is due after gharf (placing food in bowls).

When the Cook's Wage is Due: Custom as a Source of Law in Ijarah
Commentary on cook's wage due point, with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on when a hired cook's wage becomes wajib, explain the role of custom ('urf) as a legal proof, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi difference regarding the type of food.

Core Idea
A cook’s wage is due when the food is placed into bowls — custom determines the point of delivery.

You hire a cook to prepare food for a gathering. When does his work end, entitling him to his wage? The Hanafi school rules that the wage becomes wajib after the cook places the food into serving bowls (gharf). This is based on established custom ('urf), which is a valid source of law in the absence of explicit texts. In this lesson, we examine the reasoning behind this ruling and an intra-Hanafi difference about whether it applies only to wedding feasts or to all types of food.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage states that the lessor (cook) may demand wages after placing food in bowls, considering custom.
2
Note the restriction by some Hanafi scholars
Al-Quduri and others restrict this to food for a walima (wedding feast) because for household food there is no established custom.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Understand the author's broader view
The author of Al-Wiqayah left it unrestricted, listing twelve types of feasts, implying that custom applies to all.
The list includes walima, khurs, ‘aqiqa, ighdhar, hanāqa, milāk, ma’daba, wakīra, naqī‘a, wadhīḥa, and ‘atīra.
4
See how the list supports generalization
The commentator notes that walima can be generalized to any invitation feast, so the restriction is only apparent.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi position
The broader view (unrestricted) is likely mu'tamad, as it is the author's choice and supported by the generality of custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللطبخ بعد الغرف [1] (وللطبخ بعد الغرف ) [٢] زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية 11 قوله : وللطبخ الخ؛ أي وللمؤجر طلب الأجرة من المستأجر للطبخ بعد وضع الطعام في القصاع ، اعتباراً للعرف، فإنَّ المعتبر هـو الـعـادة فيما لا نص فيه ، والقُدوري وصاحب «الملتقى» (۱) وغيرهما قيدوه بأن يكون الطعام للوليمة نظراً إلى أنه لو كان لأهل بيته فلا عرف عليه للعرف. وإنما أطلقه المصنف له نظراً إلى أن للأطعمة أنواعاً : الوليمة : وهو طعام العرس، والخرس: وهو طعام الولادة. والعقيقة : وهو عند حلق شعر المولود. والإغدار : وهو طعام الختان. والحناقة : وهو الطعام عند ختم الصبي حفظ القرآن. والملاك : وهو الطعام عند التزوج. والمأدبة : وهو طعام صنع الدعوة بلا سبب. والوكيرة : وهو الطعام عند فراغ البنيان. والنقيعة : وهو طعام القادم من سفره. والوضيحة : وهو طعام المصيبة. والعتيرة : شاة كانوا يذبحونها لآلهتهم، ونظمها بعض الفضلاء، وذكر هذا النظم العلامة الطحطاوي (٢)، وغيره. والوليمة قد تعمّ كل طعام هيئ على طريق الدعوة، كما لا يخفى على من له نظر إلى المحاورات، ومن قيده بكون الطعام للوليمة نظر إلى هذا التعميم، والله عليم حكيم. [٢] قوله : بعد الغرف ؛ الغَرف بفتح الغين المعجمة وسكون الراء المهملة : إخراج المرق من القدور إلى القصاع ذكره في «المعدن» وغيره، وحاصله : جعل الطعام في القصعة، وفيه إيماء إلى أنّ تسوية الخوان ووضع القصاع واجب على الطباخ كما قيل،
And for cooking after serving [into bowls]. [1] (cooking after serving) [2] Zubdat al-Nihaya li-Umdat al-Ri'ayah 11: His statement: 'and for cooking etc.' means: the lessor may demand wages from the lessee for cooking after placing food in the bowls, considering custom (‘urf). For custom is authoritative where there is no text. Al-Quduri and the author of al-Multaqa (1) and others restricted it to when the food is for a wedding feast (walima), because if it were for his household, there is no custom regarding it. The author [may Allah have mercy on him] left it unrestricted considering that foods have types: Walima: wedding food; Khurs: food for birth; ‘Aqiqa: upon shaving the newborn’s hair; Ighdhar: food for circumcision; Hanāqa: food upon a boy completing Quran memorization; Milāk: food at marriage; Ma’daba: food prepared for an invitation without cause; Wakīra: food upon completion of building; Naqī‘a: food for a traveler returning; Wadhīḥa: food of calamity; ‘Atīra: a sheep they used to slaughter for their gods. Some virtuous person versified them, and ‘Allama al-Tahṭāwī (2) and others mentioned this versification. Walima may encompass all food prepared by way of invitation, as is clear to anyone who considers common usage. And whoever restricted it to walima did so based on this generalization. Allah is All-Knowing, Wise. [2] His statement: after serving (al-gharf): al-gharf, with a fatha on the ghayn and sukun on the ra’, means removing the broth from pots into bowls, mentioned in al-Ma‘din and others. Its essence is placing food in the bowl. In this is an indication that setting the table and placing the bowls is obligatory upon the cook, as was said.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Al-Wiqayah, expanding the ruling that a hired cook is entitled to his wage after placing the food into bowls (gharf). The commentator explains that the basis for this ruling is custom (‘urf), which is a valid source of law where no clear text exists. He notes that Al-Quduri and the author of Al-Multaqa restricted this rule to food prepared for a wedding feast (walima), arguing that for household food there is no established custom. The author of the matn, however, left it unrestricted because foods are prepared for many occasions, and he lists twelve types of feasts: walima (wedding), khurs (birth), ‘aqiqa (shaving), ighdhar (circumcision), hanāqa (Quran completion), milāk (marriage), ma’daba (invitation), wakīra (building completion), naqī‘a (traveler’s return), wadhīḥa (calamity), and ‘atīra (pre-Islamic sacrifice). The commentator then states that walima can be generalized to mean any food prepared for an invitation, which resolves the apparent restriction. Finally, he defines ‘al-gharf’ linguistically and notes that setting the table and placing bowls is obligatory upon the cook, implying the wage is due at that point.

Key Terms
الغرف (al-gharf): The act of removing broth from pots into bowls; essentially placing food into serving bowls.
العرف (al-‘urf): Established custom or practice among people, used as a source of law when no textual evidence exists.
الوليمة (al-walīma): Food prepared for a wedding feast, but can be generalized to any food prepared for an invitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a hired cook becomes entitled to his wage:
A) immediately after starting to cook.
B) after placing the food into bowls.
C) after the guests finish eating.
D) only if the food is for a wedding.

Key Takeaway
A hired cook’s wage becomes wajib when he places the food into serving bowls, based on established custom, and this ruling applies to all types of invitation feasts, not just weddings.

Wage for Brickmaking: Setting vs. Arranging
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wage timing for brickmaking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on when a brickmaker's wage is due, identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf), and apply the mufta bihi (operative) position.

Core Idea
In ijara, completion defines wage entitlement; Hanafis dispute whether brickmaking completes upon setting or only after arranging.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute about the wage of a brickmaker (ضارب اللبن). The classical Hanafi masters—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—differ on when the work is considered complete and the wage becomes obligatory. Understanding their reasoning reveals how the school defines 'completion' in service contracts and how later authorities settled the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is hiring a brickmaker to make bricks. The dispute: when is the work complete enough for the wage to be due? Note the two stages: setting (iqama) and arranging (tashrij).
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa says wage is due after setting. His reasoning: setting makes the bricks usable; arranging is extra like transport. Before setting, the clay is loose and unusable.
The work is complete at iqama.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say wage is due only after arranging (tashrij). Their reasoning: arrangement prevents spoilage; it is analogous to taking bread out of the oven—without it the product is not finished.
Tashrij is integral to completion.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If bricks spoil by rain after setting but before arranging: Abu Hanifa says wage still due; Sahibayn say not due. This shows the real-world impact.
Also applies to delivery conditions if work is on laborer's land.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Later authorities like Ibn Kamal Pasha prefer the Sahibayn's view. So for fatwa, wage is due only after arrangement.
Tarjih authority: Ibn Kamal Pasha in al-Idah and al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولضرب اللبن بعد إقامته [١]·, ولضرب اللبن بعد إقامته) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة ، وقالا (١٢) : لا يستحق حتى يشرجه ) ؛ لأن التشريح من تمام العمل، وعند أبي حنيفة ) هو زائد كالنقل وإن أفسده الطباخ أو أحرقه أو لم ينضجه فهو ضامن للطعام، وإذا أدخل الخباز أو الطباخ بنار ليخبز بها أو يطبخ بها فوقعت منه شرارة فاحترق بها البيت، فلا ضمان عليه. صرح به في «المنح»، وغيره. [١) قوله : ولضرب اللين؛ أي وللمؤجّر طلب الأجرة من المستأجر لضرب اللبن في ملك المستأجر مع تعين الملبن بعد تسويته، واللين بكسر الباء : ما يعمل من الطين ، ويبتنى به وهو بالفارسية حشت، والهندية : ابنت، والواحد لبنة. [٢]قوله : وقالا...الخ ؛ يعني وعندهما لا يستحق ضارب اللبن الأجرة إذا شرجه ، وجعل بعضه على بعض ؛ لأنّ تشريجه من تمام عمله، إذ لا يؤمن الفساد قبله، فصار كإخراج الخبز من التنور. [٣]قوله : وعند أبي حنيفة ... الخ ؛ يعني أنَّ العمل عنده قد تم بالإقامة ، والتشريج عمل زائد، كالنقل إلى موضع العمارة، بخلاف ما قبل الإقامة ؛ لأنه طين منتشر، بخلاف الخبز، فإنّه غير منتفع به قبل الإخراج. وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا فسد بمطر ونحوه بعد الإقامة، فعنده يجب الأجر، وعندهما لا يجب إلا إذا كان شرجه، وهذا إذا كان ضرب اللين في بيت المستأجر، أما إذا كان في أرض الأجير فلا يستحقها إلا بتسليمه، وهو بالعد بعد الإقامة عنده، وبالعد بعد التشريج عندهما. صرّح به الزَّيْلَعِي (٤)، وغيره. وذكر في «المستصفى» نقلاً عن «الإيضاح» و«المبسوط» إذا لم يكن في ملكه لم يكن له الأجر حتى يسلّمه منصوباً . عنده، ومشرجا عندهما . انتهى
And for striking bricks after placing them. [1] (and for striking bricks after placing them) - this according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is not entitled until he arranges them (yusharrijuhu), because arrangement (tashrij) is part of the completion of the work. According to Abu Hanifa, it is extra, like transport. And if the cook spoils, burns, or undercooks the food, he is liable for the food. And if the baker or cook enters fire to bake or cook with it, and a spark falls and burns the house, there is no liability upon him. This is explicitly stated in al-Munah and other works. [1] His statement: 'and for striking bricks' means: the lessor may demand the wage from the lessee for striking bricks on the property of the lessee, after the brickmaker is determined and the bricks are made even. Al-labin (with a kasra on the ba) is what is made from clay and built with; in Persian it is 'hasht', in Hindi 'abant', and one piece is 'libna'. [2] His statement: 'and the two said...' means: according to them, the brick striker is not entitled to the wage until he arranges them, placing some upon others, because arrangement is part of the completion of his work, since spoilage is not prevented before it, so it is like taking bread out of the oven. [3] His statement: 'and according to Abu Hanifa...' means: the work is completed by placing (iqama), and arrangement is an extra act, like transport to the construction site, unlike before placing because it is loose clay; unlike bread, which is not usable before extraction. The fruit of the disagreement appears if it spoils by rain or the like after placing: according to him the wage is due; according to them it is not due unless he had arranged it. This applies when the brick striking is in the lessee's house. If it is in the laborer's land, he is not entitled until he delivers it, which is by counting after placing according to him, and by counting after arrangement according to them. Al-Zayla‘i (4) and others explicitly stated this. And it is mentioned in al-Mustasfa quoting from al-Idah and al-Mabsut: if it is not in his possession, he does not get the wage until he delivers it erected (mansuban) according to him, and arranged (musharrijan) according to them. End.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wage of a brickmaker (ضارب اللبن) who is hired to make bricks from clay. The ruling from the matn states that the wage is due after 'setting' (إقامة) the bricks, which is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the wage is not due until the bricks are 'arranged' (تشريج), i.e., stacked or placed systematically. The commentator explains the reasoning: According to Abu Hanifa, the work is complete once the bricks are set in place; arranging them is an additional service akin to transport. According to the Sahibayn, arrangement is integral to the work because without it the bricks are prone to spoilage, analogous to how bread is not considered finished until removed from the oven. The practical difference (ثمرة الخلاف) arises if the bricks are spoiled by rain or similar after setting but before arrangement: Abu Hanifa says the wage is still due, while the Sahibayn say it is not due unless the bricks were arranged. The passage also clarifies that this dispute applies when the work is done on the hirer's premises; if on the laborer's own land, the wage is only due upon delivery. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to Ibn Kamal Pasha and others is the view of the Sahibayn, though the text notes the difference. Additionally, the passage includes rulings on liability: if a cook spoils food, he is liable; but if a baker/cook uses fire and a spark accidentally burns the house, he is not liable.

Key Terms
اللين (al-labin): Bricks made from clay; from the root 'labana' meaning to form bricks.
الإقامة (al-iqāma): Setting the bricks in place; making them stand or be positioned.
التشريج (al-tashrīj): Arranging bricks by placing some upon others; stacking or systematizing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, when does a hired brickmaker become entitled to his wage?
A) Immediately upon starting work.
B) After setting the bricks (iqama).
C) After arranging the bricks (tashrij).
D) Only after the bricks are used in construction.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on when wage is due for brickmaking, but the operative ruling is that the wage is due only after the bricks are arranged (tashrij), protecting the employer from paying for incomplete work.

The Brickmaker's Wages: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of wage entitlement for a brickmaker

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on when a brickmaker becomes entitled to wages, explain the practical difference, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A brickmaker's wages depend on what counts as completion: stacking (Abu Hanifa) or laying in the wall (Sahibayn).

This passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the moment a brickmaker's work is complete and wages become due. At stake is the definition of the contracted task and the risk of damage before delivery. We will examine the reasoning of each side and identify the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the core question
Who disagrees and about what? The dispute is between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) over when a brickmaker (ضارب اللبن) becomes entitled to wages: after stacking (إقامة) or after laying in the wall (تشريج).
2
State each position and its talil
Abu Hanifa says stacking completes the work because laying is extra like transportation. The Sahibayn say laying is integral because until placed, bricks are vulnerable to damage.
The analogy of bread not being usable until removed from the oven supports the Sahibayn.
3
Analyze the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If bricks are spoiled after stacking but before laying, Abu Hanifa says wages are due; the Sahibayn say not. This shows the impact of defining completion.
4
Examine the condition regarding the location of work
If the work is in the lessee's property, the dispute applies directly; if in the worker's own land, wages depend on delivery, which is defined differently by each (counting after stacking vs. after laying).
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative position)
Ibn Kamal Pasha in al-Idah states that fatwa is given according to the two companions (wa bi qawlihima yufta), confirmed by al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Thus, the relied-upon ruling is that wages are due after laying (tashrij).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولضرب اللبن بعد إقامته) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة ، وقالا : لا يستحق حتى يشرجه )؛ لأن التشريح من تمام العمل، وعند أبي حنيفة هو زائد كالنقل وإن أفسده الطباخ أو أحرقه أو لم ينضجه فهو ضامن للطعام، وإذا أدخل الخباز أو الطباخ بنار ليخبز بها أو يطبخ بها فوقعت منه شرارة فاحترق بها البيت، فلا ضمان عليه. صرح به في «المنح»، وغيره. [١) قوله : ولضرب اللين؛ أي وللمؤجّر طلب الأجرة من المستأجر لضرب اللبن في ملك المستأجر مع تعين الملبن بعد تسويته، واللين بكسر الباء : ما يعمل من الطين ، ويبتنى به وهو بالفارسية حشت، والهندية : ابنت، والواحد لبنة. [٢]قوله : وقالا...الخ ؛ يعني وعندهما لا يستحق ضارب اللبن الأجرة إذا شرجه ، وجعل بعضه على بعض ؛ لأنّ تشريجه من تمام عمله، إذ لا يؤمن الفساد قبله، فصار كإخراج الخبز من التنور. [٣]قوله : وعند أبي حنيفة ... الخ ؛ يعني أنَّ العمل عنده قد تم بالإقامة ، والتشريج عمل زائد، كالنقل إلى موضع العمارة، بخلاف ما قبل الإقامة ؛ لأنه طين منتشر، بخلاف الخبز، فإنّه غير منتفع به قبل الإخراج. وثمرة الخلاف تظهر فيما إذا فسد بمطر ونحوه بعد الإقامة، فعنده يجب الأجر، وعندهما لا يجب إلا إذا كان شرجه، وهذا إذا كان ضرب اللين في بيت المستأجر، أما إذا كان في أرض الأجير فلا يستحقها إلا بتسليمه، وهو بالعد بعد الإقامة عنده، وبالعد بعد التشريج عندهما. صرّح به الزَّيْلَعِي، وغيره. وذكر في «المستصفى» نقلاً عن «الإيضاح» و«المبسوط» إذا لم يكن في ملكه لم يكن له الأجر حتى يسلّمه منصوباً . عنده، ومشرجا عندهما . انتهى (۱) قال ابن كمال باشا في «الإيضاح» (۱۳۳) / (ب) : وبقولهما يفتي معزياً للـ«عيون»، وأقره صاحب الدر المختار (٥ : ١١).
And for the striking of bricks after stacking them: this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two said: he does not deserve (wages) until he lays them (in the wall); because laying is part of completing the work. And according to Abu Hanifa, it is extra, like transportation. And if the cook spoils or burns or undercooks the food, he is liable for the food. And if the baker or cook uses fire to bake or cook, and a spark falls and burns the house, there is no liability on him. Stated clearly in al-Manh and others. [1] His statement: 'and for striking bricks' means: the lessor can demand the wage from the lessee for striking bricks in the lessee's property, when the bricks are made after leveling. 'Labin' (with kasra on ba) is what is made from clay and built with, in Persian 'khesht', in Hindi 'eent', the singular is 'labinah'. [2] His statement: 'and the two said' etc. means: according to them, the brickmaker does not deserve wages if he laid them, placing some on others; because laying is part of his complete work, since corruption before it is not safe, so it is like taking bread out of the oven. [3] His statement: 'according to Abu Hanifa' etc. means: according to him, the work is completed by stacking, and laying is extra work, like transporting to the construction site, unlike before stacking because it is spread mud, unlike bread because it is not beneficial before removal. The practical consequence appears if it is spoiled by rain etc. after stacking: according to him wages are due, according to them not unless he laid them. This is if the brick striking is in the lessee's house; but if in the worker's own land, he does not deserve wages until delivery, which by counting after stacking according to him, and by counting after laying according to them. Stated by al-Zayla'i and others. And mentioned in al-Mustasfa quoting from al-Idah and al-Mabsut: if not in his ownership, he does not get wages until he delivers it set up (according to Abu Hanifa) or laid (according to the two). End. (1) Ibn Kamal Pasha said in al-Idah: And by their statement fatwa is given, attributed to al-Uyun, and agreed by the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar (5:11).
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding when a brickmaker becomes entitled to his wages. The core issue is whether stacking the bricks (i.e., forming them but not yet placing them in the wall) completes the work. According to Abu Hanifa, the work is complete by stacking (iqama), and placing them in the wall (tashrij) is an additional task like transportation. Therefore, wages are due after stacking. The two companions hold that placing is integral to the work because until placed, the bricks are vulnerable to damage (e.g., rain), so wages are only due after placement. The practical difference (thamara) arises if the bricks are spoiled after stacking but before placement: Abu Hanifa says wages are due, the two say not. The passage then notes two conditions: (1) if the work is in the lessee's property, the dispute applies; (2) if in the worker's own land, wages depend on delivery, which is determined differently by each view. Additionally, a related ruling is given: a cook or baker is liable for spoiling the food but not for fire damage caused by a spark from his fire, unless he was negligent. The commentary quotes Ibn Kamal Pasha stating that the fatwa is given according to the two companions, as confirmed by al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Key Terms
ضرب اللبن (darb al-labin): The work of making bricks from clay and stacking them.
إقامة (iqama): Stacking the formed bricks upright to dry, considered by Abu Hanifa as completion of the work.
تشريج (tashrij): Laying the bricks in the wall, placing some upon others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa in the Hanafi school, when does a brickmaker become entitled to his wages?
A) Immediately after mixing the clay.
B) After stacking the bricks (iqama).
C) After laying the bricks in the wall (tashrij).
D) Only after the bricks are delivered to the owner.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a brickmaker's wages are due only after laying the bricks in the wall (tashrij), as per the preferred position of the two companions.

Worker's Right to Detain Object for Wages (Haql al-Habs)
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on a worker's right to detain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a Hanafi worker may detain an object for wages, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the school's preferred definition of 'trace'.

Core Idea
A worker may detain an object only if his work leaves a trace by attaching his own property to it.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every worker who performs a service on an object is entitled to detain that object until paid. The key is whether the work leaves a 'trace' (athar) in the object. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies that right and presents a significant intra-Hanafi dispute over its scope and the consequences if the object perishes while detained.

Guided Path
1
Identify the worker and his right
Read the opening: the worker whose work leaves a trace in the object (like a dyer) has the right to detain (habs) the object for his wages. Note the analogy to sale.
The right is conditional, not absolute.
2
Understand the analogy to sale
The author states that because the contracted work is a quality that remains in the object, the worker's right to detain is like a seller's right to withhold goods until payment.
This is a form of lien (haql al-habs).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability
If the detained object perishes without the worker's fault: Imam Abu Hanifa says no liability and no wage; the Sahibayn give the owner a choice between paying the wage with compensation for the enhanced value, or not paying the wage and compensating only the original value.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is risk allocation.
4
Examine the definition of 'trace'
The passage then reports two opinions from al-Qunyah: (1) trace means the worker's own property (like starch, dye) attaches to the object; (2) trace means any observable change (like grinding). The author chooses the first. Apply this to a fuller: no right unless he uses owned starch or eggs.
This definition determines who gets the right of detention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لعمله أثر في العين كصباغ [۱] [۲] زبدة النهاية لعمدة الرعاية ومَن لعمله أثر في العين : أي شيء من ماله قائم بتلك العين، كالصبغ مثلاً ، كصباغ [1] قوله : ومن لعمله.... الخ ؛ يعني ومن كان بعمله أثر في العين كصباغ يظهر لوناً في الثوب، وقصار يقصر بالنشا والبيض. فللمستأجر حبس تلك العين لأجل الأجرة حتى يستوفيها ؛ لأنَّ المعقود عليه وصف قائم في الثوب، فله حق الحبس لاستيفاء البدل كما في البيع، فإن حبسها للأجرة فضاعت العين بلا تعد منه فلا ضمان عليه ؛ لكونه أمانةً في يده، كما كان قبل الحبس، ولا أجر له إذا هلك المعقود عليه قبل التسليم، وهذا عند الإمام. وقالا : إن شاء المالكُ ضَمَّنَه مصبوغاً ، وله الأجر ؛ لأنَّ العمل صار مسلماً إليه تقديراً لوصول قيمته إليه، فصار كما لو صار مسلّماً حقيقة، أو غير مصبوغ، ولا أجر له ؛ لأنَّ العمل لم يصر مسلماً إليه. [٢]قوله : أي شيء من ماله...الخ ؛ في «القنية»: اختلف المشايخ في قول أصحابنا كل صانع لعمله أثر في العين فله حبسها للأجر، فقيل : المراد به الأجزاء المملوكة للصانع التي تتصل بمحل العمل، كالنشاشتج والغرا والحنوط ونحوها، وهو مختار صاحب «المحيط». وقيل : مجرد ما يرى ويعاين في محل العمل، ككسر الفستق والحطب، وطحن الحنطة، وحلق رأس العبد، وهو مختار قاضي خان، وظهير الدين التمرتاشي. انتهى كلامه ومختار المصنف . هو القول الأول، فعلى هذا لا يكون للقصار ولاية الحبس إذ هو لم يخلط ملكه بالثوب ، إلا إذا قصر بالنشاشتج أو ببياض البيض ؛ لأنه اتصل به ملكه. وعلى القول الثاني يكون له ولاية الحبس ؛ لأنه لما غلب الوسخ على الثوب ، واستتر البياض به صارَ في حكم المعدوم، وحين أظهر القصار لعمله، وجعل ظهوره مضافاً إلى عمله، فيكون أثر عمله قائماً في المعمول. كذا في «شرح النقاية» للعلامة البرْجَندِي.
And whoever has a trace of his work in the object, like a dyer. [1] [2] Zubdat al-Nihayah li 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah: And whoever has a trace of his work in the object: meaning anything of his property that remains in that object, like dye for example, like a dyer. [1] His statement: 'and whoever his work has a trace...' etc. means: whoever's work leaves a trace in the object, like a dyer who shows a color in the cloth, and a fuller who fulls with starch and eggs. Then the lessee (worker) has the right to detain that object for the wage until he receives it; because the contracted matter is a quality that remains in the cloth, so he has a right of detention to collect the payment, as in sale. If he detains it for the wage and the object perishes without his transgression, there is no liability on him because it is a trust in his hand, as it was before detention. And he has no wage if the contracted object perishes before delivery, and this is according to the Imam. And the two said: if the owner wishes, he may hold him liable for the dyed (value) and he gets the wage; because the work is considered delivered virtually due to reaching its value, so it is as if actually delivered. Or he may (hold liable) for undyed (value) and he gets no wage; because the work was not delivered to him. [2] His statement: 'anything of his property...' etc. In al-Qunyah: The scholars differed about our companions' statement: every artisan whose work has a trace in the object has the right to detain it for the wage. Some said: what is meant is the parts owned by the artisan that become attached to the work, like starch, glue, perfume, etc. This is the choice of the author of al-Muhit. Others said: merely what is seen and observed in the work, like cracking pistachio, splitting wood, grinding wheat, shaving a slave's head. This is the choice of Qadi Khan and Zahir al-Din al-Tamurtashi. End of his words. And the author's choice is the first opinion. So on this basis, the fuller has no right of detention because he did not mix his property with the cloth, unless he fulls with starch or egg white because his property attaches. On the second opinion, he has the right of detention because when dirt overcomes the cloth and whiteness is concealed, it becomes as if non-existent. And when the fuller shows his work and makes its appearance attributable to his work, then the trace of his work is present in the worked object. Thus in Sharh al-Niqayah by al-Barjandi.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal ruling for a worker (like a dyer or fuller) whose work leaves a trace in the object. The key point is that such a worker may detain the object until his wages are paid, because the contracted work is a quality that now inheres in the object. This right of detention (habs) is analogous to a seller's right to withhold goods until payment. If the detained object perishes without the worker's fault, he is not liable because it is a trust (amanah) in his hands. If the object perishes before delivery, the worker loses his wages. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa. The two companions (Sahibayn) give the owner a choice: either hold the worker liable for the enhanced value (including the work) and pay the wage, or hold him liable for the original value and not pay the wage. The passage then delves into a secondary issue: what exactly constitutes 'a trace of work in the object'? Two opinions are cited from al-Qunyah. The first (chosen by the author) says it refers to parts owned by the artisan that become attached, like starch, glue, etc. The second says it includes any observable effect, like cracking nuts or grinding grain. The author's choice is the first, so a fuller who only uses water has no right of detention unless he uses starch or eggs. This shows the careful delineation of rights in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
أثر في العين (athar fi al-ayn): A trace of the worker's work that remains in the object, either by adding his own property or by transforming its condition.
حق الحبس (haqq al-habs): The right of the worker to detain the object until his wages are paid.
قصار (qassar): A fuller, one who cleans and presses cloth, sometimes using starch or eggs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's chosen opinion in the passage, under what condition does a fuller have the right to detain the cloth for his wages?
A) When he has fulled the cloth with water only.
B) When he has used starch or eggs that become attached to the cloth.
C) Whenever he has performed any work on the cloth.
D) Only if the cloth perishes in his possession.

Key Takeaway
A worker may detain an object for wages only if his work leaves a trace by attaching his own property to it; without that, there is no right to detain.

Fuller's Right to Detain Item for Wages
Explaining fuller's detention right and Zufar dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule on a fuller's right to detain and evaluate Zufar's opposing argument.

Core Idea
A fuller may detain the item for his wage because the work requires attachment by necessity, so consent to delivery is not implied.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the Hanafi position on a fuller's right to detain the item for his wages. It also presents the objection of Imam Zufar and the Hanafi response, illustrating the school's use of necessity as a legal principle. The lesson focuses on the legal reasoning (talil) behind the ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the dissenter
State the Hanafi position: the fuller has the right to detain the item for his wage if the wage is immediate. Identify the dissenter: Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) who denies this right.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school, not between madhhabs.
2
State the dissenter's proof
Zufar argues that the work becomes attached to the owner's property with his permission, so delivery is complete and the right to detention falls. He analogizes to sowing another's field with one's own seed.
Zufar's analogy is based on the idea of possession by connection.
3
State the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the attachment is out of necessity; the owner's consent is not truly given because the work cannot exist without attachment. The analogy with sowing is distinguished because the sower's action is voluntary, while the fuller's work requires attachment by necessity.
The text compares to the owner of an upper floor building the lower floor out of necessity.
4
Identify the thamarah (practical consequence)
Zufar rules no right to detain, and if the item perishes while with the fuller, he is liable. Abu Hanifa rules the fuller has the right to detain, and if it perishes, he is not liable (trust) and also loses the wage because the work was not delivered.
The thamarah shows the difference in liability and entitlement.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text sides with Abu Hanifa's position, and it is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school. The condition for detention is that the wage must be immediate; if deferred, no detention is allowed.
The ruling is conditional: only if the wage is due and payable immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[١]قوله : للأجر ؛ إذا كان حالاً ، أما إذا كان الأجر مؤجلاً فلا يملك حبسها ؛ لأن التسليم ليس الواجب عليه للحال، فلا يملك الحبس، كما لو باع شيئاً بثمن مؤجل ليس له الحبس. كذا في «المنح»، وغيره. [٢] قوله : فلا غرم ولا أجر ؛ أما عدم وجوب الضمان ؛ فلأنّ العين أمانة في يده عند الإمام، وكان له أن يحبسها بالأجرة شرعاً، فلا يكون به متعدّياً، فلا وجه لوجوب الضمان، وأما عدم وجوب الأجر ؛ فلأنَّ المعقود عليه هلك قبل التسليم ، وهو موجب لسقوط البدل، كما أن المبيع إذا هلك قبل القبض سقط الثمن.
Book of Ijarah, Chapter: When Wages are Due. And a fuller who fullens with starch and eggs has the right to detain them for the wage. [1] His saying: 'who fullens' etc.: This is in Syria, to make the hidden whiteness appear, and similarly the ruling of a fuller who fullens with clear water as in our land. Mentioned in 'Majma' al-Anhur'. [2] His saying: 'with starch': starch like hasa: pleasant scent, and starch like kalam what is made from wheat, Ibn al-Jawaniqi said: its origin is nashastaj, the Persians say nashasta, so it remained shortened, and in the speech of some authors: the Arabs used it long, and the shortened is generated, and Tha'lab said: al-nasha' is long. As in 'al-Misbah al-Munir'. [3] His saying: 'and eggs': of a bird and its like lays eggs, so it is laying, and eggs for it are like offspring for animals, plural of bayd is buyud, singular baydah, plural baydat with sukun of ya, and Hudhayl open it by analogy. As in 'al-Misbah'. [4] His saying: 'detaining them for the wage': and Zufar said: he does not have the right to detain them because the subject of the contract has been delivered to the owner of the item by its connection to his property, so the right of detention falls, for the connection to his property only occurred with his permission, so it becomes like possession by hand; thus if a man ordered another to sow his land with wheat as a loan, and the one ordered sowed it, he becomes a possessor by connection to his property, and becomes like if he dyed in the house of the hirer. And the answer: The connection of the work to the place is a necessity for performing the work, so he was not consenting to this connection in terms of it being a delivery, rather his consent is in realizing the work of dyeing and similar effect in the place, for the work has no existence except by it, so he was compelled to it, and consent is not established with compulsion. Do you not see that the owner of the upper floor if he builds the lower floor, he is not considered a volunteer or consenting because he is compelled to it, and the analogy on dyeing in the house of the hirer is an analogy with a difference due to his possession of the house. (1) Restricted to both because his work has a trace, and excludes the washer of clothes. See 'Durar al-Hukkam' (2:227). (2) 'Majma' al-Anhur' (2:373). (3) 'al-Misbah al-Munir' (2:936). (4) 'al-Misbah al-Munir' (1:110). Page 526. Zubdat al-Nihayah li 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah. For the wage. [1] [2] For the wage, then if he detains and it perishes, there is no liability and no wage. [1] His saying: 'for the wage': if it is immediate, but if the wage is deferred, he does not have the right to detain it, because delivery is not obligatory upon him immediately, so he does not have the right to detention, just as if he sold something for a deferred price, he does not have the right to detain. Thus in 'al-Minah' and others. [2] His saying: 'no liability and no wage': as for the absence of liability, because the item is a trust in his hand according to the Imam, and he had the right to detain it for the wage legally, so he is not transgressing, so there is no basis for liability; and as for the absence of wage, because the subject of the contract perished before delivery, which necessitates the fall of the exchange, just as if the sold item perishes before possession, the price falls.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the ruling of a fuller's right to detain the item for wages. The author begins by defining the fuller (قصار) who uses starch and eggs, typical in Syria to whiten fabric, and notes that fullers using clear water have the same ruling. Lexical explanations are given: 'starch' (نشا) is a type of whitener, with a detailed etymology; 'eggs' (بيض) are like offspring for birds. The central ruling: the fuller may detain the item for the wage. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that the work becomes attached to the item with the owner's consent, thus delivery is complete and the right to detention falls. He compares to a case where a person sows another's land with his own wheat by order—the sower becomes possessor. The Hanafi response is that the attachment is necessary for the work to exist, so consent is not truly given; the owner is compelled. An analogy with a person building a lower floor for an upper owner shows compulsion negates consent. The dyeing analogy is distinguished because the dyer does not have possession of the house. The commentary then specifies that the wage must be immediate (حال) for the right to detain; if deferred, no detention is allowed. If the item perishes while detained, there is no liability because the item is a trust, and no wage because the work was not delivered (like a sold item perishing before possession).

Key Terms
النشا (al-nasha): A substance like starch used for stiffening and whitening clothes; in this context, used by fullers.
البيض (al-bayd): Eggs, used by fullers in Syria to whiten fabric.
قصار (qassar): A fuller or launderer who whitens and presses clothes.
حبس (habs): Detention of an item as a lien for payment due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a fuller lawfully detains the item for an immediate wage and the item perishes?
A) He is liable for the value and still entitled to the wage.
B) He is not liable and his wage is forfeited.
C) He is not liable and still entitled to the wage.
D) He is liable for half the value and half the wage.

Key Takeaway
A fuller may detain the item for an immediate wage because the work attachment is by necessity, but if the item perishes lawfully detained, he is not liable but loses his wage.

Worker with No Trace Cannot Detain Item: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on detention and liability for workers with no trace

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on liability when a worker with no trace detains the item and it perishes, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A porter’s work leaves no trace, so detention is invalid; liability depends on whether the item was guaranteed before detention.

This passage examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute regarding workers whose work leaves no physical trace on the item, such as porters. The core question: if such a worker detains the item for unpaid wages and it perishes, is he liable? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, reach different conclusions based on the underlying status of the item as a trust or guaranteed. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the rules of ijarah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the worker category
Recognize that the ruling applies to workers like porters, sailors, and washers, whose work does not alter or add a physical trace to the item. This is the key condition for the dispute.
Contrast with workers like fullers (who leave a trace) – they may detain.
2
State Abu Hanifa’s position
According to Abu Hanifa, if such a worker detains the item and it perishes, he is not liable (no ghurm) and loses his wage (no ujrah). The item remains a trust (amanah) in his hand.
Rationale: The worker had no right to detain, but the item’s trust status is unchanged.
3
State the Sahibayn’s position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the item was guaranteed (mamnun) before detention, so it remains guaranteed after. The hirer has a choice: either claim value without work (no wage) or with work (pay wage).
Rationale: The worker was not entrusted with the item; detention is akin to wrongful possession.
4
Analyze the reasoning
The difference stems from whether the item is considered a trust due to the hire contract (Abu Hanifa) or whether the absence of authorization makes the worker a guarantor (Sahibayn). The text also notes that the worker could avoid this by working at his own premises.
The expansion probe explains why detention is inconceivable: the work is an accident with no permanent trace.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the hirer gets no compensation and pays no wage. Under the Sahibayn, the hirer can choose between two options. This affects how a mufti advises parties.
Later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn in matters of liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَن لا أثر لعمله كالحمال ا، فإن حبس فضاعَ فلا غرمَ ولا أجر )) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة الله ، وعندهما : العين كانت مضمونة قبل الحبس ، فكذا بعده ، ثم هو بالخيار عندهما ، إن شاء ضمَّنَهُ قيمته غير معمول ، ولا أجرَ له ، وإن شاءَ ضمنه معمولا وله الأجر. ( ومن لا أثر لعمله ) : أي ليس شيءٌ من ماله قائماً بتلك العين ، كالحمال) والعامل يمكن أن يحترز عنه بأن يعمل في منزل نفسه، فلا يكون مضطراً إليه، فلا جرم أن يكون راضياً بالتسليم مع إمكان التحرز عنه، فيبطل حقه في الحبس، كما إذا سلم المبيع برضاه، فليس له حق الاسترداد ).
ثم [٣] قوله : ومن لا أثر...الخ ؛ يعني وكلُّ صانع ليس لعمله أثر في العين كالحمال والملاح وغاسلُ الثوب ليس له أن يحبس العين للأجرة ؛ لأنَّ المعقود عليه هو نفس العمل، وهو عرض ولا له أثر يقوم مقامه ، فلا يتصوَّر حبسه.
،
ولو حبس تلك العين ،فضاعت، ضمن ضمان الغصب، وصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء ضَمَّنَ المستأجر قيمتها محمولة، وله الأجر، وإن شاء غير محمولة، ولا أجر له. صرّح به في «الجوهرة».
[٤]قوله : كالحمال ؛ - بالحاء المهملة - ، للمبالغة مأخوذاً من الحمل ، يقال : حملت المتاع حملاً ، من باب ضرب فهو حامل ، وفي بعض النسخ بالجيم، بمعنى سائقِ الجمل،
And whoever's work has no trace, like the porter, if he detains and it perishes, there is no liability and no wage. This according to Abu Hanifa. And according to them (the two disciples): the item was guaranteed before detention, so likewise after, then he has the choice, if he wishes he is made liable for its value without work, and no wage for him, and if he wishes he is made liable for it worked and he has the wage. (And whoever's work has no trace): meaning there is nothing of his property standing in that item, like the porter. And the worker can avoid this by working in his own house, so he is not compelled, so inevitably he is consenting to delivery with the possibility of avoidance, so his right to detention is void, just as if he delivered the sold item with his consent, he has no right to reclaim. Then [3] His saying: 'And whoever's work has no trace' etc.: meaning every craftsman whose work has no trace in the item, like the porter, the sailor, and the washer of clothes, does not have the right to detain the item for the wage, because the subject of the contract is the work itself, which is an accident and has no trace that can stand in its place, so detention is inconceivable. And if he detains that item and it perishes, he is liable for usurpation (ghasb), and the owner has the choice: if he wishes, he makes the hirer liable for its value as carried, and he has the wage, and if he wishes, as not carried, and no wage for him. This is explicitly stated in 'al-Jawharah'. [4] His saying: 'like the porter' (al-hammal) with an unpointed ha, for exaggeration derived from haml (carrying), it is said: hamaltu al-mata'a hamlan, from the chapter of daraba, so he is haamil. In some copies it is with jim, meaning the driver of a camel.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage is a expansion probe on the ruling for workers whose work leaves no tangible trace on the item, such as a porter (who carries goods), a sailor, or a washer of clothes. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, such a worker cannot detain the item for wages; if he does and the item perishes, he is not liable and loses his wage, because the item was a trust in his hand and detention was not legally justified. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they hold that the item was guaranteed (mamnun) before detention (since the worker is not entrusted with it), so it remains guaranteed after detention. They give the hirer a choice: either to claim the value of the item without the work (i.e., as if not carried) and forfeit the wage, or to claim it with the work (i.e., the value after carrying) and pay the wage. The commentary explains that the reason such workers cannot detain is that their work has no physical residue in the item; the contract is for the act of work itself, which is ephemeral and cannot be 'detained'. The worker can avoid this situation by performing the work on his own premises, where he has control, thus avoiding the risk. The author then cites a different view from 'al-Jawharah': if such a worker does detain and the item is lost, he is liable for ghasb (usurpation), and the owner has the option to claim the value with or without the work. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa's view is that there is no liability (the item is a trust), while the Sahibayn see liability. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is not explicitly stated here, but the text seems to present both.

Key Terms
حمال (hammal): A porter or carrier whose work has no physical trace on the item carried.
لا أثر لعمله (la athar li-'amalihi): His work leaves no trace in the item, i.e., it does not alter or add anything to the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a porter detains the item and it perishes, what options does the hirer have?
A) The hirer can only claim the value without work and forfeit the wage.
B) The hirer can only claim the value with work and pay the wage.
C) The hirer can choose between claiming the value without work (no wage) or with work (pay wage).
D) The hirer can claim the full value and also demand the porter pay a penalty.

Key Takeaway
A worker with no trace on the item cannot detain it for wages; Abu Hanifa says no liability, the Sahibayn say the hirer has a choice; later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn.

Porter's Detention and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Liability and Wage
Intra-Hanafi dispute on porter's liability after detention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on a porter's liability and wage when he detains the hired animal for immediate wage and it perishes, and explain the legal reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
A porter who detains for wage is not a transgressor under Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn split liability and wage.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya confronts a practical conflict: a porter detains the hired animal to secure his wage, but the animal perishes. The base text gives a single ruling, but the commentator reveals a deep split within the Hanafi school between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute requires grasping the legal nature of the worker's possession (amana vs. guarantee) and how it affects liability and wage entitlement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal actors and the incident
The case involves a porter (ḥammāl) who detains the hired animal (e.g., donkey) to enforce payment of his immediate wage (ajr ḥālan). The animal then perishes. Note the key elements: worker, subject matter (animal), detention (ḥabs), wage, and loss.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules: no liability (lā gharam) and no wage (lā ajr). Reason: the animal is an amana (trust) in the porter's hand, and he had the legal right (sharʿan) to detain for the wage, so he is not a transgressor. The wage drops because the subject matter perished before delivery, analogous to a sale perishing before delivery (al-mabīʿ idhā halaka qabla l-qabḍ saqaṭa th-thaman).
Underlying principle: lawful detention preserves the trust status.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the object was already under guarantee (maḍmūna) before detention (because the worker's initial possession was not a trust), so after detention it remains guaranteed. The owner (rabb al-māl) has a choice: either hold the porter liable for the value without work (qīmatuhu ghayra maʿmūl) and pay no wage, or hold him liable for the value with work (maʿmūlan) and pay the wage.
The owner's option reconciles the guarantee with the worker's claim to wage.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the porter bears no loss but forfeits his wage; the owner absorbs the full loss. Under Sahibayn, the owner can recover either the animal's value (without wage) or the value plus wage. The financial outcomes differ sharply, illustrating the real-world impact of the legal characterization.
The dispute hinges on whether the pre-detention possession was amana (trust) or guarantee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للأجر، فإن حبس فضاعَ فلا غرمَ ولا أجر، ومَن لا أثر لعمله كالحمال ا، فإن حبس فضاعَ فلا غرمَ ولا أجر )) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة الله ، وعندهما : العين كانت مضمونة قبل الحبس ، فكذا بعده ، ثم هو بالخيار عندهما ، إن شاء ضمَّنَهُ قيمته غير معمول ، ولا أجرَ له ، وإن شاءَ ضمنه معمولا وله الأجر. ( ومن لا أثر لعمله ) : أي ليس شيءٌ من ماله قائماً بتلك العين ، كالحمال) والعامل يمكن أن يحترز عنه بأن يعمل في منزل نفسه، فلا يكون مضطراً إليه، فلا جرم أن يكون راضياً بالتسليم مع إمكان التحرز عنه، فيبطل حقه في الحبس، كما إذا سلم المبيع برضاه، فليس له حق الاسترداد ). (۲) [١]قوله : للأجر ; إذا كان حالاً ، أما إذا كان الأجر مؤجلاً فلا يملك حبسها ; لأن التسليم ليس الواجب عليه للحال، فلا يملك الحبس، كما لو باع شيئاً بثمن مؤجل ليس له الحبس. كذا في «المنح»، وغيره. [٢] قوله : فلا غرم ولا أجر ; أما عدم وجوب الضمان ; فلأنّ العين أمانة في يده عند الإمام، وكان له أن يحبسها بالأجرة شرعاً، فلا يكون به متّعدياً، فلا وجه لوجوب الضمان، وأما عدم وجوب الأجر ; فلأنَّ المعقود عليه هلك قبل التسليم ، وهو موجب لسقوط البدل، كما أن المبيع إذا هلك قبل القبض سقط الثمن.
For the wage: if he detains and it perishes, then no guarantee and no wage. And the one whose work leaves no trace, like the porter: if he detains and it perishes, then no guarantee and no wage. This is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. But according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the object was under guarantee before detention, so likewise after. Then the owner has a choice: if he wishes, he may hold him liable for its value without work and no wage; if he wishes, he may hold him liable for it worked and give him the wage. (And the one whose work leaves no trace): meaning nothing of his property subsists in that object, like the porter. The worker can avoid this by working in his own house, so he is not compelled; therefore he is satisfied with delivery while he could avoid it, so his right to detention is void, just as if the seller delivered the sold good willingly, he has no right to reclaim. (2) [1] He said: For the wage; if it is due immediately, but if the wage is deferred, he does not have the right to detain it because delivery is not obligatory on him immediately, so he does not have the right to detain, just as if he sold something for a deferred price, he does not have the right to detain. Thus in al-Manh and others. [2] He said: So no guarantee and no wage; as for the non-obligation of guarantee, because the object is a trust in his hand according to Imam, and he had the right to detain it for the wage legally, so he is not a transgressor, so there is no basis for liability. As for the non-obligation of wage, because the subject matter of the contract perished before delivery, which necessitates the dropping of the consideration, just as if the sold item perishes before delivery, the price drops.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya is a commentary on al-Wiqaya, addressing the case of a porter (ḥammāl) who detains the animal he rented for transport to secure his wage. The author first presents the ruling as stated in the base text: if he detains and the animal perishes, he is not liable (fā ḍāʿa fā lā gharama wa lā ajr). This is 'at Abī Ḥanīfa, meaning Abu Hanifa's position. Then the commentator explains that the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, referred to as 'inda humā) differ: they consider the object (al-ʿayn) as already under guarantee (maḍmūna) before detention because the worker's possession was not a trust; thus after detention it remains guaranteed. The owner has a choice: either claim the value of the animal as if untouched (qīmatahu ghayra maʿmūl) and no wage, or claim the value with the work done (maʿmūlan) and pay the wage. The commentary further explains the reason for no liability under Abu Hanifa: the animal is an amāna (trust) in the worker's hand, and since he had the legal right to detain for the wage, he is not a transgressor (mutāddin). The wage drops because the subject matter perished before delivery, analogous to a sale where the item perishes before delivery cancels the price. Additionally, a condition is noted: the wage must be immediately due (ḥālan) for the right to detain; if deferred (mu'ajjalan), no detention right exists, likened to a deferred price sale.

Key Terms
الأجر (al-ajr): The wage for the hired work; conditionally gives right to detain if presently due.
الحبس (al-ḥabs): Detention of the subject matter (e.g., animal) by the worker to enforce payment of wage.
الحمال (al-ḥammāl): Porter; one who carries goods, often on an animal. His work leaves no trace in the article carried.
أمانة (amāna): Trust; property held without liability for loss unless by transgression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The owner must bear the loss and pay the wage.
B) The owner can choose to claim the value of the animal without work and not pay the wage, or claim the value with work and pay the wage.
C) The owner can only claim the value of the animal without work.
D) The owner cannot claim anything because the detention was legal.

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, a porter who detains for immediate wage and the animal perishes is not liable under Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn give the owner a choice between liability with or without wage.

Workers Without Trace Cannot Detain; Exception for Finder of Runaway Slave
Ruling with proof: who cannot detain for wages and why, with an exception for finder of runaway slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing workers who may detain property for wages and justify the exception for the finder of a runaway slave using its proof (saving from destruction).

Core Idea
Only workers whose labor leaves a trace may detain; the finder of a runaway slave is an exception because he saves the slave from destruction.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi fiqh: which workers have the right to detain the subject matter of their contract for unpaid wages? The passage defines workers whose work leaves no trace (like porters and boatmen) and explains why they cannot detain. It also discusses the special case of the finder of a runaway slave, who does have the right to detain, and notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement with Zufr. Understanding this distinction is critical for correctly applying rulings on liens and wage claims in hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its basis
The passage states that any artisan whose work leaves no trace in the object (e.g., porter, boatman, washer for cleaning) has no right to detain the object for the wage. The reason: the subject matter of the contract is the work itself, which is an accident (ʿaraḍ) and does not subsist in the object, so detention is conceptually impossible.
The trace (athar) is a physical alteration or improvement; carrying does not alter the object.
2
List the examples given
Three examples are provided: the porter (ḥammāl), the boatman (mallāḥ), and the washer of cloth (ghāsil al-thawb) when washing only for cleaning (taṭhīr), not improvement. These workers' labor does not create a lasting trace.
The washer is distinguished: if washing aims at improvement (taḥsīn), then the work does leave a trace and he may detain.
3
Understand the consequence of wrongful detention
If such a worker detains the object and it perishes, he is liable as a usurper (ḍamān al-ghaṣb). The owner has a choice: claim the value with the work (and pay the wage) or claim the value without work (and no wage).
This ensures the worker does not benefit from his wrongful act.
4
Analyze the exception for the finder of a runaway slave
The base text states: 'unlike the finder of a runaway slave' – he may detain the slave for the reward (juʿl). The proof: the slave was on the verge of destruction (ʿalā sharaf al-halāk), so returning him is like reviving him; the reward is like a sale price.
This exception is based on analogy to sale (qiyas) or istihsan, as the finder's action is akin to purchasing.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Zufr holds that even the finder of a runaway slave cannot detain, whether his work leaves a trace or not. The passage does not provide a response, but the majority view (as implied) is that he can. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
The practical consequence: under the majority view, the finder can hold the slave until paid; under Zufr, he must return and sue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٣] قوله : ومن لا أثر لعمله...الخ ; يعني وكلُّ صانع ليس لعمله أثر في العين كالحمال والملاح وغاسلُ الثوب ليس له أن يحبس العين للأجرة؛ لأنَّ المعقود عليه هو نفس العمل، وهو عرض ولا له أثر يقوم مقامه ، فلا يتصوَّر حبسه. ولو حبس تلك العين ،فضاعت، ضمن ضمان الغصب، وصاحبها بالخيار إن شاء ضَمَّنَ المستأجر قيمتها محمولة، وله الأجر، وإن شاء غير محمولة، ولا أجر له. صرّح به في «الجوهرة». [٤]قوله : كالحمال ; - بالحاء المهملة - ، للمبالغة مأخوذاً من الحمل ، يقال : حملت المتاع حملاً ، من باب ضرب فهو حامل ، وفي بعض النسخ بالجيم، بمعنى سائقِ الجمل، (1) ينظر: «التبيين»(٥ : ١١١). (۲) «منح الغفار (۲ : ۲۳۳ /ب). والملاح وغاسل الثوب لا حبس له ، بخلافِ راد الآبق، فإنَّ الآبق كان على شرف الهلاك، فكأنه أحياه، وباع منه بالجعل، وعند زفر ه ليس له حق الحبس سواء كان لعمله أثر في العين أو لا. [١] قوله : والملاح ؛ بالتشديد السفان، وهو الذي يجري السفينة في البحر. [٢] قوله : وغاسل الثوب ; أي لتطهيره لا لتحسينه، فإنّه إذا كان يغسل لتحسينه فله حق الحبس ، قال في «البحر»: أطلقه فشمل أو إذا لم يكن لعمله إلا إزالة الدرن بالغسل فقط على الأصح ; لأنَّ البياض كان مستتراً ، وقد ظهر بفعله، فكأنه أحدثه فيه. انتهى. [٣]قوله : بخلاف راد الآبق ; يعني بخلافِ راد الآبق فإنّه يحبسه على الجعل، وإن لم يكن لعمله أثر ; لأنه كان على شرف الزوال والهلاك، فأحياه بالرد ، فكأنه باعه، فكان له حق الحبس.
[3] He said: 'And the one whose work leaves no trace...' meaning every artisan whose work leaves no trace in the object, like the porter, boatman, and washer of cloth, does not have the right to detain the object for the wage, because the subject matter of the contract is the work itself, which is an accident and has no trace that stands in its place, so detention is inconceivable. If he detains that object and it perishes, he is liable as a usurper, and its owner has a choice: if he wishes, he may hold the lessee liable for its value carried (i.e., with the work) and he has the wage; if he wishes, for its value not carried, and no wage. This was explicitly stated in al-Jawhara. [4] He said: 'like the porter' – with an unpointed ḥā, for intensification derived from ḥaml (carrying); it is said: ḥamaltu al-matāʿa ḥamlan, from the paradigm ḍaraba, so he is ḥāmil; in some copies it is with jīm, meaning a camel-driver. (1) Refer to al-Tabyīn (5:111). (2) Minḥ al-Ghaffār (2:233/b). And the boatman and washer of cloth have no right to detain, unlike the finder of a runaway slave; for the slave was on the verge of destruction, so it is as if he revived him, and sold to him by reward. According to Zufr, he has no right to detain whether his work leaves a trace in the object or not. [1] He said: 'the boatman' – with tashdīd, the sailor, who drives the ship at sea. [2] He said: 'and the washer of cloth' – meaning for cleaning, not for improvement; if he washes for improvement, he has the right to detain. He said in al-Baḥr: 'He made it absolute, so it includes even if his work only removes dirt by washing on the correct view, because the whiteness was hidden and it has appeared by his action, as if he created it in it.' End. [3] He said: 'unlike the finder of a runaway slave' – meaning unlike the finder of a runaway slave, for he detains him for the reward, even if his work has no trace, because the slave was on the verge of perishing and destruction, so he revived him by returning, as if he bought him, so he has the right to detain.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on al-Wiqaya. It first defines 'man lā athara li-ʿamalihi' (one whose work leaves no trace) as including the porter (ḥammāl), boatman (mallāḥ), and washer of cloth (ghāsil al-thawb) for cleaning (taṭhīr). Such workers cannot detain the subject matter (e.g., the animal or clothes) for their wage because the subject matter of the contract is their work (al-ʿamal), which is an accident (ʿaraḍ) that does not subsist in the object. Detention is therefore not conceivable. If they do detain and the object perishes, they are liable as usurpers (ḍamān al-ghaṣb), and the owner has a choice: either claim the value with the work (i.e., as if the work had been done) and pay the wage, or claim the value without work and not pay the wage. This is from al-Jawhara. The commentator then explains the word 'ḥammāl' (porter) noting it is with ḥā, from carrying, but some copies have jīm (jammāl) meaning camel-driver. Then the base text states: 'al-mallāḥ wa ghāsil al-thawb lā ḥabsa lahu, bikhilāfi rādd al-ābiq' (the boatman and washer of cloth have no detention, unlike the finder of a runaway slave). The commentary explains that the boatman (mallāḥ) is the sailor, and the washer of cloth (ghāsil al-thawb) is for cleaning, not improvement; if the washing aims at improvement (taḥsīn), then the washer does have a right to detain because his work creates value (the whiteness becomes apparent). That is the correct view, as in al-Baḥr. The exception for rādd al-ābiq (finder of a runaway slave) is because the slave was on the verge of destruction, so by returning him, the finder is like one who revives and sells, thus he has a right to detain for the reward (juʿl). The passage also notes that according to Zufr (a Hanafi scholar), the finder does not have the right to detain, whether his work leaves a trace or not. This shows an intra-Hanafi disagreement, though Imam Muhammad's view is the one given as the relied-upon.

Key Terms
أثر (athar): Trace; evidence of the worker's labor in the object, such as shaping or improving it.
راد الآبق (rādd al-ābiq): The finder of a runaway slave who returns him to his owner and is entitled to a reward.
ضمان الغصب (ḍamān al-ghaṣb): Liability arising from usurpation; the wrongful possession of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following workers does NOT have the right to detain the subject matter for his wage?
A) A tailor who sews a shirt.
B) A washer who cleans clothes for improvement.
C) A porter who carries goods on an animal.
D) A finder of a runaway slave.

Key Takeaway
Only workers whose labor creates a tangible, lasting improvement can detain; the finder of a runaway slave is a special exception due to the slave's peril.
