وفيها أجر المثل لا يزاد على المسمى

قوله : وفيها أجر المثل...الخ ; يعني إنَّ الواجب في الإجارةِ الفاسدة هو : المثل لا يجاوز به المسمّى، وهذا إذا لم يكن الفساد لجهالة المسمّى أو لعدم التسمية، فإن كان لجهالة المسمّى أو لعدم التسمية يجب أجر مثلِهِ بالغا ما بلغ.
وكذا إذا كان بعضه معلوماً وبعضه غير معلوم، مثل أن يسمي دابة أو ثوباً أو يستأجر الدار أو الحمام على أجرة معلومة بشرط أن يعمرها أو يرممها، وقالوا : إذا استأجر داراً على أن [لا] يسكنها المستأجر فسدت الإجارة ، ويجب عليه إن سكنها أجرُ المثل بالغاً ما بلغ. ذكره العيني)، وغيره.
وعند زفر والشافعي له يجب بالغاً ما بلغ ، كما في البيع الفاسد تجب قيمة العين بالغة ما بلغت.
ولنا : أن المنافع غير متقومة بنفسها بل بالعقد، وقد أسقطا الزيادة فيه.

قوله : وعند زفر ... الخ ; يعني وقال زفر والشافعي وكذا مالك وأحمد : يجب أجر المثل في الإجارة الفاسدة بالغاً ما بلغ ؛ لأنَّ المنافع متقومةُ ، وقد تعدَّرَ إيجاب المسمى للفساد، فيجب المصير إلى القيمة، كما أنّ البيع إذا فسد وجبت القيمة بالغة ما بلغت، وهذا بناء على أن المنافع كالأعيان عندهم. [٢) قوله : ولنا: إن...الخ ; يعني ولنا : إنّ المنافع لا تتقوم بنفسها ؛ لأن التقوم يستدعي سبق الإحراز، والمنافع لا تبقى وكل ما لا يبقى لا يحرز، وإنما تصير متقومة بالعقد شرعاً ؛ لضرورة حاجة الناس إليها، والضروري يتقيد بالضرورة، والضرورة تندفع بالإجارة الصحيحة دون الفاسدة، فيكتفي بها. إلا أن الفاسد من كل عقد يلحق بصحيحه ؛ لأنَّ الفاسد مشروع بأصله دون وصفه، وفي تميزه عن الصحيح حرج ، فيعتبر في الفاسد من الإجارة ما يعتبر في صحيحها من البدل، وهو أجر المثل إلا أنَّ المتعاقدين إذا اتفقا على مقدار فقد أسقط الزيادة، وإذا نقص أجرُ المثل لم تجب زيادة المسمى بفساد التسمية.
والجواب عن قياس زفر والشافعي : إن العين تتقوم بنفسها، والقيمة هو الموجب الأصلي، فإن صحت التسمية انتقل الواجب عن الموجب الأصلي إلى المسمّى والا فلا.
And in it (invalid lease) is the equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl), but not increased beyond the named wage. He said: 'The statement occurs: 'and in it is the equivalent wage...' means that what is obligatory in an invalid lease is the equivalent wage, not exceeding the named wage, and this is when the invalidity is not due to ignorance of the named wage or lack of naming. If it is due to ignorance of the named wage or lack of naming, then its equivalent wage is due, whatever it amounts to. Likewise, if part is known and part unknown, such as naming an animal or a garment, or renting a house or bathhouse for a known wage on condition that the lessee repairs or renovates it. They said: If one rents a house on condition that the tenant does not live in it, the lease is invalid, and if he lives in it, he must pay the equivalent wage, whatever it amounts to. Al-‘Ayni and others mentioned this. And according to Zufar and al-Shafi‘i, it is due whatever the amount, just as in an invalid sale the value of the object is due, whatever it amounts to. And our proof: Benefits are not valuable in themselves but only through the contract, and they (the parties) have waived the increase in it.

He said: 'And according to Zufar... etc.' means that Zufar, al-Shafi‘i, and also Malik and Ahmad say: The equivalent wage in an invalid lease is due whatever the amount, because benefits are valuable, and since the named wage cannot be made obligatory due to invalidity, one must resort to the value, just as in an invalid sale the value is due whatever it amounts to. This is based on their view that benefits are like physical objects. [2] He said: 'And our proof is that...' means our proof is that benefits are not valuable in themselves, because being valuable requires prior acquisition, and benefits do not endure, and whatever does not endure cannot be acquired. They only become valuable through a valid contract by law, due to people's need for them, and what is necessary is limited to the extent of necessity. Necessity is satisfied by a valid lease, not an invalid one, so the valid suffices. However, every invalid contract is attached to its valid counterpart because the invalid is legislated in its origin but not in its description, and distinguishing it from the valid causes hardship. So in an invalid lease, what is considered in the valid lease regarding the substitute (badal) is considered, which is ajr al-mithl, except that if the parties agreed on an amount, they have waived any excess. If ajr al-mithl is less, the named wage is not increased due to the invalidity of the naming. And the response to the analogy of Zufar and al-Shafi‘i: Physical objects are valuable in themselves, and value is the original obligation. If the naming is valid, the obligation transfers from the original to the named; otherwise, it does not.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the obligation of ajr al-mithl (equivalent wage) in an invalid ijarah contract. The matn states the Hanafi ruling: ajr al-mithl is due but cannot exceed the named wage (al-musamma). The commentary first clarifies exceptions: if the invalidity is due to ignorance of the named wage or lack of naming, then ajr al-mithl is due without limit. Similarly, if part of the wage is known and part unknown, the limit does not apply. Then the dispute is presented: Zufar (a Hanafi scholar), al-Shafi‘i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that ajr al-mithl is due without any cap, drawing an analogy to invalid sale where the value of the object is paid without limit. The Hanafi response is that benefits (manafi‘) are not inherently valuable like physical objects; they become valuable only through a valid contract. Since the parties have mutually agreed on a specific wage (al-musamma), they have implicitly waived any amount above it. The exception is when the named wage is unknown—then there is no waiver. The commentary also explains the principle that an invalid contract is treated like a valid one in terms of the substitute, but the agreed amount is respected. The Hanafi argument is based on istihsan (juristic preference) over the qiyas of the opponents.

Key Terms
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The market rate or equivalent wage for similar benefits in a lease.
المسمى (al-musamma): The named or agreed wage stipulated in the contract.
المنافع غير متقومة (al-manafi‘ ghayr mutaqawwimah): Benefits are not independently valuable (unlike physical objects).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when is ajr al-mithl due without a cap in an invalid ijarah?
A) Always
B) When the invalidity is due to ignorance of the named wage (jahalat al-musamma) or lack of naming
C) When the lessor has already received the benefit
D) When the named wage is higher than the market rate

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school limits ajr al-mithl in invalid ijarah to the agreed wage unless the wage itself is unknown, based on the principle that benefits become valuable only through contract and parties waive excess.

Leasing a House per Month: Ruling on Validity
Stating the ruling on a lease contract for a house per month

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a lease contract phrased as 'each month' and explain why it is valid only for the first month based on the principle of jahalah.

Core Idea
A lease for an indefinite term is invalid except for the first definite month – uncertainty voids the rest.

This lesson examines a common but problematic lease phrasing: renting a house 'each month' (kull shahr). The Hanafi school holds that such a contract is valid only for the first month and void for the rest, because the total term is unknown. In Fiqh, uncertainty (jahalah) in the essential terms of a contract invalidates it. Here, the word 'kull' implies generality and an endless series, making the subsequent months indefinite. Understanding this ruling helps you apply the general rule that lease terms must be clearly specified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and the issue
The contract is an ijarah (lease) of a house where the term is expressed as 'kull shahr' (each month). The issue is whether such a phrasing creates a valid lease for multiple months or not.
2
Understand the application of 'kull'
The word 'kull' is a tool of generality (umum). Applied literally, it would encompass an infinite number of months. Since months have no natural end, this leads to jahalah (ignorance) of the total period.
Ja'alah is a defect that makes a contract fasid (invalid) in Hanafi law.
3
Determine validity for the first month
The first month is definite and known; therefore, the contract is sahih (valid) for that one month. For the remaining months, the term is unknown, so the contract is fasid.
The ruling is not total invalidity but partial: valid for the first, invalid for the rest.
4
State the legal consequence
The lessor is entitled to rent for the first month only. If the tenant occupies beyond that, the lessor may claim fair market rent (ujrat al-mithl) for the subsequent months, but not the contracted rent for those months because the contract is null for them.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح إجارة

قوله : وصح ...الخ ; يعني من استأجر داراً كلّ شهر هكذا صح العقد في شهر واحد فقط، وفسد في الباقي إذ لا يمكن تصحيح العقد على جملة الشهور لجهالتها ، والأصل أن لفظ : كلّ ; موضوع للعموم ، وقد تعذر العمل به ؛ لأن الشهور لا نهاية لها، والواحد معين، فيصح فيه.
And the lease is valid. He said: 'The statement occurs: 'and valid... etc.' means that if one rents a house each month like this, the contract is valid for only one month, and invalid for the rest, because it is not possible to validate the contract for the totality of the months due to their ignorance. The principle is that the word 'each' (kull) is placed for generality, but it cannot be applied here because months have no end, while one month is definite, so it is valid in that.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding a specific lease scenario: renting a house 'each month' (kull shahr). The commentary explains that the contract is valid only for the first month and invalid for the subsequent months. The reason is the word 'kull' (each) implies generality and an indefinite number of months, leading to jahalah (ignorance) regarding the total term. Since the months are unlimited in theory, the contract cannot be enforced beyond the first definite month. This ruling is based on the principle that leases for an indefinite period are invalid due to uncertainty. The contract is therefore sahih (valid) for the first month only, and fasid (invalid) for the rest.

Key Terms
كل شهر (kull shahr): A phrase meaning 'each month' – used to indicate a recurring monthly lease without specifying an end date.
العموم (al-‘umum): Generality; the word 'kull' denotes all-inclusiveness, but here it cannot be applied because it would make the term indefinite.
الجهالة (al-jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty in a contract term that leads to invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The contract is valid for the first month only.
C) The contract is valid for all months if the lessee pays monthly.
D) The contract is valid only if the parties intend a specific number of months.

Key Takeaway
A lease with an indefinite term is valid only for the first definite period; uncertainty (jahalah) in the term invalidates the remainder.

Compensation in Voidable Lease: Hanafi vs. Opponents
Dispute regarding compensation in voidable lease and a subsidiary ruling on duration uncertainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on compensation in a voidable lease (ijara fasida), explain the Hanafi evidence based on the nature of benefits (manafi'), and apply the ruling to determine the amount due when named rent differs from market rate.

Core Idea
In a voidable lease, the named rent binds as a cap – benefits are not intrinsically valuable.

This passage presents a key inter-madhhab dispute about what compensation is owed when a lease contract is voidable (fasid). The Hanafi school argues that the agreed rent (musamma) serves as a cap, while Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad insist that the market rate (ujr al-mithl) must be paid regardless. Understanding this difference relies on a deeper principle: whether benefits (manafi') are considered property (mutaqawwima) or merely contractual rights. The passage also introduces a subsidiary ruling about leases with uncertain duration to test the boundaries of the principle.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on compensation
Identify that the Hanafi school holds the named rent as binding: if the named rent is less than the market rate, only the named rent is due; if it exceeds the market rate, the market rate is due.
The named rent acts as a cap, not a floor.
2
Identify the opponent's position and their analogy
Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad analogize to a voidable sale (bay' fasid), where the full market value of the commodity (qimah al-'ayn) is owed. They argue that benefits are like physical assets and thus require market compensation.
Opponents treat benefits as mutaqawwima (property).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that benefits are not intrinsically valuable (ghayr mutaqawwima bi nafsiha) but acquire value through the contract. Since the parties agreed to a specific rent, they have waived any excess (asqata al-ziyadah). In voidable sale, the asset itself can be returned; benefits cannot be returned, so the agreed compensation stands.
The distinction rests on the nature of benefits vs. physical assets.
4
Apply the rule to the subsidiary case
Examine the lease 'each month for such-and-such' where the total duration is undefined. The Hanafi ruling: valid only for the first month; for subsequent months it is void unless the lessee resides for the first hour of each month with consent, then it becomes valid for that month. The principle of certainty in duration is tested here.
This subsidiary case illustrates that uncertainty in duration invalidates the lease except by subsequent agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند زفر والشافعي له يجب بالغاً ما بلغ ، كما في البيع الفاسد تجب قيمة العين بالغة ما بلغت.
ولنا : أن المنافع غير متقومة بنفسها بل بالعقد، وقد أسقطا الزيادة فيه.
وصح إجارة دار كل شهر بكذا في واحدٍ فقط، وفي كلِّ شهر سكن ساعة في أوله، وفي كل شهر إِن عُلِمَ مدته
And according to Zufar and al-Shafi'i, the compensation [in a voidable lease] becomes obligatory in whatever amount it reaches, just as in a voidable sale the value of the commodity is obligatory in whatever amount it reaches. And for us [the Hanafis]: benefits are not intrinsically valuable; rather they become valuable through the contract, and the two [parties] have already waived the increase [beyond the named rent]. And the lease of a house 'each month for such-and-such' is valid only for one month, and for each month if he resides for the first hour of it, and for each month if its duration is known.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage contains a dispute between the Hanafi school and the schools of Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad regarding the compensation owed when a lease contract is invalid (fasid). The opponents argue that the lessee must pay the market rate (ujr al-mithl) regardless of any named rent, because benefits are considered property (muttaqawwima) like physical assets. They analogize to a voidable sale where the full market value of the item is due. The Hanafi position is that benefits are not intrinsically valuable; they only acquire value through a valid contract. In a voidable lease, the named rent (musamma) serves as the agreed compensation, and since both parties consented to that amount, any excess is waived. However, if the named rent exceeds the market rate, the excess is void, and only ujr al-mithl is due. This is based on istihsan: treating the invalid lease as much like a valid lease as possible, while avoiding hardship. The text then states a subsidiary ruling: if someone leases a house for an unspecified number of months by saying 'each month for such-and-such,' the lease is valid only for the first month; for subsequent months it is void due to uncertainty. But if the lessee actually resides for the first hour of each subsequent month with consent, the lease becomes valid for that month. If the total duration is known, e.g., 'six months, each month for a dirham,' the entire lease is valid by consensus.

Key Terms
إجارة فاسدة (ijara fasida): A lease contract that is defective in its description (such as uncertainty in duration) but valid in its essence; it is not prohibited but lacks full validity.
أجر المثل (ujr al-mithl): The market rent for a similar property in similar conditions, used as a benchmark when the named rent is absent or excessive.
متقومة (mutaqawwima): Having monetary value in the eyes of the law; property that is owned and can be sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a voidable lease, what is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions?
A) The Hanafi school requires payment of the named rent only if it is less than the market rate; otherwise market rate.
B) The Hanafi school always requires the market rate; the Shafi'i school always requires the named rent.
C) The Hanafi school requires the market rate if the named rent exceeds it; the Shafi'i school requires the named rent regardless.
D) The Hanafi school requires the named rent; the Shafi'i school requires the market rate regardless.

Key Takeaway
In a voidable lease, the Hanafi school binds compensation by the named rent as a cap, based on the principle that benefits are not intrinsically valuable and parties' agreement waives excess.

Ruling on Per-Month Rental: Validity and Cancellation Right
Ruling on per-month rental with hourly occupancy at start

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a rental contract with per-month rent and hourly occupancy, and identify the mufta bihi timeframe for cancellation.

Core Idea
A rental contract with per-month rent and hourly occupancy is valid but each party can cancel in the first night and day of each month.

This lesson examines a specific ijarah scenario where the rent is set per month but the total duration is ambiguous. The Hanafi school rules it valid, relying on custom (urf) to define the cancellation window. You will learn why the manifest transmission (zahir al-riwaya) considers the first night and day as the beginning of the month, not the exact hour of the crescent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract scenario and its ambiguity
The contract: 'a house for each month for a certain amount, and in each month he occupies for an hour at its beginning.' The total duration is not specified. This ambiguity raises the question of validity.
The matn uses 'fi wahid faqat' indicating only one month is considered if duration unknown.
2
Understand the two views on cancellation timing
Some mashayikh (qiyas) hold cancellation at the exact hour of the crescent; the manifest transmission (zahir al-riwaya) holds it during the first night and day. The latter is mufta bihi.
The commentator explains that considering the exact hour would cause hardship (haraj).
3
Analyze the dalil from Kitab al-Ayman
Imam Muhammad's example: a person swears to repay a debt at the 'beginning of the month' and repays in the first night and day; he does not break his oath by istihsan. This shows that 'beginning of the month' customarily includes the first night and day.
This is a qawl sahabi used as evidence for custom.
4
Identify the mufta bihi position and its basis
The commentator states 'wa bihi yufta' for the zahir al-riwaya position. The basis is custom ('urf) and istihsan to avoid hardship.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.
5
Note the consequence: each party has a temporary cancellation right
Once the first night and day pass, the contract becomes binding for that month. At the beginning of the next month, the right renews.
If total duration is specified (e.g., six months), the contract is valid by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة / باب الإجارة الفاسدة
دار كل شهر بكذا في واحدٍ فقط، وفي كلِّ شهر سكن ساعة في أوله، وفي كل شهر إِن عُلِمَ مدته

[٢] دار كل شهر بكذا في واحد فقط، وفي كلِّ شهر سكن ساعةً في أوله)، هذا عند بعض المشايخ، فإنه حين يهل الهلالُ يكون لكل واحد حق الفسخ، فإذا مضى أدنى زمان لزم العقد في هذا الشهر، وفي ظاهر الرواية لكل منهما حق الفسخ في الليلة الأولى مع اليوم الأول من الشهر إذ في اعتبار أن رؤية الهلال ج)، ( وفي كلِّ شهر إن عُلِمَ مدته)، بأن قيل: أجرت ستة أشهر كل شهر بكذا.

وفي قول عن الشافعي: يبطل.
وعند مالك: يصح في الكل، وبه قال أحمد في رواية، وأشار بقوله: فقط إلى أنه لا يصح أكثر من شهر، ثم إذا تم الشهر كان لكل منهما نقض الإجارة، بشرط أن يكون الآخر حاضراً، وإن كان غائباً لا يجوز بالإجماع، وقيل: لا يجوز عندهما إلا بحضرة الآخر. وعند أبي يوسف يجوز، أما إذا عين كل الأشهر بأن يقول: أجرتها عشرة أشهر، كل شهر بدرهم مثلاً صح العقد فيها بالإجماع لكون المدة معلومة.

[1] قوله: وفي كل شهر ... الخ؛ يعني وكل شهر سكن المستأجر منه ساعةً صح فيه العقد لحصول رضائها بذلك.
[٢] قوله: هذا عند بعض المشايخ؛ وهو القياس، فإن رأس كل الشهر في الحقيقة هو الساعة التي يهل فيها الهلال، فإذا أهل مضى رأس الشهر فلا يمكن الفسخ.
(۳) قوله: وفي ظاهر الرواية لكل منهما ... الخ؛ وبه يفتى؛ لأن في اعتبار الساعة حرجاً عظيماً، والمقصود هو الفسخ في رأس الشهر، وهو عبارة عن الليلة الأولى ويومها عرفاً.
ألا ترى إلى ما ذكره محمد في كتاب الأيمان: فمن حلف ليقضين دين فلان رأس الشهر فقضاه في الليلة التي يهل فيها الهلال وفي يومها لم يحنث استحساناً.
(۱) وبه يفتى. كما في تبيين الحقائق (٥:١٢٣)، ومجمع الأنهر (٢:٣٨٢)، والدر المنتقى (٢:٣٨٢)، وغيرها.
Book of Ijarah / Chapter of Invalid Ijarah
A house for each month for such amount in only one, and in each month he occupies for an hour at its beginning, and in each month if its duration is known.

[2] ('A house for each month for such amount in only one, and in each month he occupies for an hour at its beginning') This is according to some mashayikh: when the crescent appears, each has the right to cancel, and when a minimal time passes, the contract becomes binding for that month. And in the manifest transmission (zahir al-riwaya), each of them has the right to cancel in the first night along with the first day of the month, due to considering... (and in each month if its duration is known), meaning if it is said: I rented six months each month for such amount.

And in a statement from al-Shafi'i: it is invalid.
According to Malik: it is valid in all, and Ahmad said so in one narration. He indicated by his words 'only' that it is not valid for more than one month. Then when the month is completed, each has the right to rescind the lease, on condition that the other is present. If absent, it is not permissible by consensus. It is said: it is not permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) except in the presence of the other. According to Abu Yusuf: it is permissible. But if he specified all the months, saying: I leased it for ten months, each month for a dirham, the contract is valid by consensus because the duration is known.

[1] His saying: 'And in each month...' etc.; meaning each month the lessee occupies from it for an hour, the contract is valid therein due to obtaining mutual consent.
[2] His saying: 'This is according to some mashayikh'; and it is analogy (qiyas), for the beginning of each month in reality is the hour when the crescent appears, so when it appears, the beginning of the month has passed and cancellation is not possible.
(3) His saying: 'And in the manifest transmission each of them...' etc.; and by this fatwa is given, because considering the hour would be extremely difficult, and the intended meaning is cancellation at the beginning of the month, which is the first night and its day according to custom.
Do you not see what Muhammad (al-Shaybani) mentioned in Kitab al-Ayman: Whoever swears to repay the debt of so-and-so at the beginning of the month, and repays it in the night when the crescent appears and its day, he does not break his oath by istihsan.
(1) And by this fatwa is given. As in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (5:123), Majma' al-Anhur (2:382), al-Durr al-Muntaqa (2:382), and others.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in rental contracts where the rent is set per month but the total duration is ambiguous. The matn states: if someone rents a house for each month for a certain amount, but only for one month (في واحد فقط), and it is stipulated that in each month the tenant will occupy only for an hour at the beginning, then the ruling depends on whether the overall duration is known. The commentator explains that according to some mashayikh, when the crescent appears signaling a new month, each party has the right to cancel the lease. However, in the manifest transmission (zahir al-riwaya) from Imam Muhammad, the right to cancel is restricted to the first night and day of the month. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) because considering the exact hour of the crescent would cause hardship. The commentator also mentions the views of other schools: al-Shafi'i holds the contract invalid, while Malik and Ahmad consider it valid in all cases. Importantly, if the total duration is specified (e.g., six months), the contract is valid by consensus. The passage also discusses conditions for cancellation: both parties must be present, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf allows it even in absence. This ruling highlights the Hanafi principle of istihsan in preferring custom over strict analogy, as demonstrated by the oath example from Imam Muhammad's Kitab al-Ayman. The lesson concludes with the statement that fatwa is given according to the manifest transmission.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The manifest transmission of the Hanafi school from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
رأس الشهر (Ra's al-Shahr): The beginning of the month, which customarily includes the first night and day.

Cancellation Conditions and Cross-Madhhab Comparison
Cancellation conditions and cross-madhhab comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi difference on cancellation presence and compare the Hanafi ruling with the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali positions.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require both parties present for cancellation; Abu Yusuf permits it even absent, and other schools differ on validity.

This lesson delves into the conditions for cancellation in the per-month rental scenario. Within the Hanafi school, there is a disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other. Additionally, Imam al-Shafi'i declares such contracts invalid due to gharar, while Malik and Ahmad validate them. Understanding these differences clarifies the practical application of the Hanafi mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Recall the Hanafi ruling on the contract's validity and cancellation timeframe.
The contract is valid but each party has the right to cancel in the first night and day of each month (zahir al-riwaya).
This is the mufta bihi position from the previous lesson.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on cancellation condition: presence of both parties.
The text states: 'bishart an yakun al-akhar hadiran' (condition that the other is present). Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold this condition; Abu Yusuf allows cancellation even if the other party is absent.
The difference is based on the interpretation of need and analogy.
3
Note the majority view vs. Abu Yusuf's view.
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) require presence; Abu Yusuf's view is more lenient. The commentator does not specify which is mufta bihi here, but the absence of a tarjih suggests presence requirement is relied upon.
This is an ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Compare with Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali positions.
Shafi'i: the contract is invalid due to gharar. Malik and Ahmad (in one narration): the contract is valid in all cases without cancellation conditions.
The thamarah al-khilaf is significant: Shafi'i makes the contract batil; Hanafi makes it sahih with a cancellation right; Maliki/Hanbali make it unconditionally valid.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf and the tarjih.
The practical difference: under Shafi'i, no contract exists; under Hanafi, the contract exists but can be cancelled periodically; under Maliki/Hanbali, it is fully binding. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi among Hanafis, but the presence condition is part of the school's ruling.
The Hanafi response to Shafi'i's objection is that uncertainty is resolved by the right to cancel.

[٢] دار كل شهر بكذا في واحد فقط، وفي كلِّ شهر سكن ساعةً في أوله)، هذا عند بعض المشايخ، فإنه حين يهل الهلالُ يكون لكل واحد حق الفسخ، فإذا مضى أدنى زمان لزم العقد في هذا الشهر، وفي ظاهر الرواية لكل منهما حق الفسخ في الليلة الأولى مع اليوم الأول من الشهر إذ في اعتبار أن رؤية الهلال ج)، ( وفي كلِّ شهر إن عُلِمَ مدته)، بأن قيل: أجرت ستة أشهر كل شهر بكذا.

وفي قول عن الشافعي: يبطل.
وعند مالك: يصح في الكل، وبه قال أحمد في رواية، وأشار بقوله: فقط إلى أنه لا يصح أكثر من شهر، ثم إذا تم الشهر كان لكل منهما نقض الإجارة، بشرط أن يكون الآخر حاضراً، وإن كان غائباً لا يجوز بالإجماع، وقيل: لا يجوز عندهما إلا بحضرة الآخر. وعند أبي يوسف يجوز، أما إذا عين كل الأشهر بأن يقول: أجرتها عشرة أشهر، كل شهر بدرهم مثلاً صح العقد فيها بالإجماع لكون المدة معلومة.

[٢] قوله: هذا عند بعض المشايخ؛ وهو القياس، فإن رأس كل الشهر في الحقيقة هو الساعة التي يهل فيها الهلال، فإذا أهل مضى رأس الشهر فلا يمكن الفسخ.
(۳) قوله: وفي ظاهر الرواية لكل منهما ... الخ؛ وبه يفتى؛ لأن في اعتبار الساعة حرجاً عظيماً، والمقصود هو الفسخ في رأس الشهر، وهو عبارة عن الليلة الأولى ويومها عرفاً.

Book of Ijarah / Chapter of Invalid Ijarah
A house for each month for such amount in only one, and in each month he occupies for an hour at its beginning, and in each month if its duration is known.

[2] ('A house for each month for such amount in only one, and in each month he occupies for an hour at its beginning') This is according to some mashayikh: when the crescent appears, each has the right to cancel, and when a minimal time passes, the contract becomes binding for that month. And in the manifest transmission (zahir al-riwaya), each of them has the right to cancel in the first night along with the first day of the month, due to considering... (and in each month if its duration is known), meaning if it is said: I rented six months each month for such amount.

And in a statement from al-Shafi'i: it is invalid.
According to Malik: it is valid in all, and Ahmad said so in one narration. He indicated by his words 'only' that it is not valid for more than one month. Then when the month is completed, each has the right to rescind the lease, on condition that the other is present. If absent, it is not permissible by consensus. It is said: it is not permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) except in the presence of the other. According to Abu Yusuf: it is permissible. But if he specified all the months, saying: I leased it for ten months, each month for a dirham, the contract is valid by consensus because the duration is known.

[1] His saying: 'And in each month...' etc.; meaning each month the lessee occupies from it for an hour, the contract is valid therein due to obtaining mutual consent.
[2] His saying: 'This is according to some mashayikh'; and it is analogy (qiyas), for the beginning of each month in reality is the hour when the crescent appears, so when it appears, the beginning of the month has passed and cancellation is not possible.
(3) His saying: 'And in the manifest transmission each of them...' etc.; and by this fatwa is given, because considering the hour would be extremely difficult, and the intended meaning is cancellation at the beginning of the month, which is the first night and its day according to custom.
Do you not see what Muhammad (al-Shaybani) mentioned in Kitab al-Ayman: Whoever swears to repay the debt of so-and-so at the beginning of the month, and repays it in the night when the crescent appears and its day, he does not break his oath by istihsan.
(1) And by this fatwa is given. As in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq (5:123), Majma' al-Anhur (2:382), al-Durr al-Muntaqa (2:382), and others.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in rental contracts where the rent is set per month but the total duration is ambiguous. The matn states: if someone rents a house for each month for a certain amount, but only for one month (في واحد فقط), and it is stipulated that in each month the tenant will occupy only for an hour at the beginning, then the ruling depends on whether the overall duration is known. The commentator explains that according to some mashayikh, when the crescent appears signaling a new month, each party has the right to cancel the lease. However, in the manifest transmission (zahir al-riwaya) from Imam Muhammad, the right to cancel is restricted to the first night and day of the month. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) because considering the exact hour of the crescent would cause hardship. The commentator also mentions the views of other schools: al-Shafi'i holds the contract invalid, while Malik and Ahmad consider it valid in all cases. Importantly, if the total duration is specified (e.g., six months), the contract is valid by consensus. The passage also discusses conditions for cancellation: both parties must be present, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; Abu Yusuf allows it even in absence. This ruling highlights the Hanafi principle of istihsan in preferring custom over strict analogy, as demonstrated by the oath example from Imam Muhammad's Kitab al-Ayman. The lesson concludes with the statement that fatwa is given according to the manifest transmission.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The manifest transmission of the Hanafi school from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
رأس الشهر (Ra's al-Shahr): The beginning of the month, which customarily includes the first night and day.

Yearly Lease with Lump Sum and Start of Term
Ruling on yearly rent without monthly breakdown and start of term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a yearly lease without specifying monthly installments and identify when the lease term begins if no date is specified.

Core Idea
A yearly lease is valid with a lump sum; the term begins at contract if unspecified.

When renting a property for a year with a single lump sum, does the contract need to break down the monthly rent? The Hanafi school says no, as long as the total duration is certain. Similarly, the start of the lease term follows the parties' specification, and if none, it begins at the moment of contract. This lesson explores these two practical issues and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a yearly lease (ijara) with a single lump sum. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) even without specifying the monthly rent.
The key is that the total duration (year) is known, which removes any harmful uncertainty (gharar).
2
Understand the condition for validity
The condition is that the total duration of the lease must be known. The monthly breakdown is not required because the total is fixed and the rent can be apportioned equally.
Analogous to a one-month lease where daily breakdown is not needed.
3
Apply the ruling on rent division
Once the contract is valid, the total rent is divided equally over the months. Seasonal price fluctuations do not affect the apportionment.
This ensures predictability and avoids disputes.
4
Determine the start of the term
If the parties specify a start date (e.g., 'from Ramadan'), that date is binding. If not, the term begins at the time the contract is made.
Just as an oath to not speak for a month begins from the day of the oath.
5
Distinguish from similar rulings in worship
Unlike a vow to fast, which does not automatically start from the following day because fasting is restricted to daytime, a lease can begin at any time, so the immediate following time is taken.
This contrast highlights how commercial contracts follow ease and custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإجارتها سنةً بكذا وإن لم يسمّ قسط كلّ شهر، وأوّل المدة ما سمّي، وإلا فوقت العقد

قوله: وإجارتها...الخ؛ عطف على قوله: إجارة الدار؛ أي وصح إجارة الدار سنة بعشرة دراهم مثلاً، وإن لم يبين قسط كل شهر من الأجرة؛ لأن المدة معلومة بدون التقسيم، فصار كإجارة شهر واحد، فإنه جائز، وإن لم يبين قسط كل يوم. فإذا صح وجب أن يقسم الأجر على الأشهر على السواء، ولا يعتبر تفاوت الأسعار باختلاف الزمان.

[٢] قوله: وأول المدة...الخ؛ يعني ابتداء مدة الإجارة ما سمي إن وقعت التسمية بأن يقول: من شهر رمضان من هذه السنة، وإن لم يقع التسمية فوقت العقد، هو المعتبر في ابتداء المدة؛ لأن الأوقات كلها متساوية بالنسبة إلى ذلك العقد. فإن كل الأوقات محل للإجارة لعدم المنافاة بين الإجارة وبين وقت ما أصلاً، فتعين الزمان الذي يعقبه، كما إذا حلف لا يكلم فلاناً شهراً، فيعتبر ابتداءه من يوم الحلف. بخلاف ما إذا نذر أن يصوم شهراً حيث لا يتعين الشهر الذي يلي النذر؛ لأن الصوم يختص ببعض الأوقات، فإن الليل ليس بمحل له، فلا يتعين ما يعقب سببه، وإن بين المدة تعين ذلك، وهو ظاهر.
And renting it for a year for such amount even if he does not specify the installment of each month, and the beginning of the term is what is specified, otherwise the time of the contract.

His saying: 'And renting it...' etc.; it is connected to his saying: 'Renting the house'; meaning: the renting of the house for a year for ten dirhams, for example, is valid even if he does not clarify the installment of each month from the rent, because the duration is known without division, so it becomes like renting for one month, which is permissible, even if he does not clarify the installment of each day. So if it is valid, then the rent must be divided equally over the months, and the variation of prices due to different times is not considered.

[2] His saying: 'And the beginning of the term...' etc.; meaning: the start of the lease term is what is specified if a specification is made, such as saying: from the month of Ramadan of this year, and if no specification is made, then the time of the contract is considered in determining the start of the term, because all times are equal with respect to that contract. For all times are suitable for lease due to there being no incompatibility between lease and any time at all, so the time that follows it is determined, just as if someone swears not to speak to so-and-so for a month, then the start is considered from the day of the oath. Unlike if he vows to fast for a month, where the month following the vow is not determined, because fasting is specific to certain times, for the night is not suitable for it, so what follows its cause is not determined, and if he specifies the duration, that is specified, and this is apparent.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues in rental contracts: (1) the validity of a yearly lease with a lump sum rent, and (2) determining the start of the lease term. The commentator clarifies that if the total duration is known (e.g., one year), the contract is valid even if the monthly breakdown is not specified. The rent is then divided equally among the months, regardless of seasonal price fluctuations. This is analogous to renting for a single month: the daily breakdown is not required. The second issue concerns the start date. If the parties specify a start date (e.g., from Ramadan), that is binding. If no date is specified, the term begins from the time of contract. This is because all times are equally suitable for lease. The commentator draws an analogy with an oath: if one swears not to speak for a month, the month starts from the day of the oath. In contrast, fasting is restricted to daytime, so a vow to fast for a month does not automatically start from the following day; it requires specification. This highlights the Hanafi principle that commercial contracts (mu'awadat) are based on custom and ease, unlike acts of worship which have specific rulings.

أول المدة (Awwal al-mudda): The beginning of the lease term.

Key Takeaway
A yearly lease with a lump sum is valid in Hanafi fiqh, and the rent is divided equally over the term; if no start date is specified, it begins at the time of contract.

Cancellation During the Month Takes Effect at Month's End
Ruling on effect of lease cancellation announced mid-month

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on lease cancellation announced mid-month and distinguish between the primary view and the fatwa of Muhammad ibn Salam.

Core Idea
Cancelling a monthly lease mid-month does not end it until the month's end; the cancellation is deferred to the correct time.

This passage examines the effect of cancellation (faskh) announced during a rental month. The main principle is that cancellation does not take effect immediately because the right to cancel exists only at the month boundaries. A secondary view holds that cancellation can be effective at month's end by alignment. Understanding this ruling illustrates the Hanafi concept of idafah (deferment) applied to contract termination.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the case: a party cancels a monthly lease in the middle of the month. The primary ruling is that the cancellation does not take effect immediately; it is deferred until the end of the month.
2
Locate the ikhtilaf
Note the alternative view attributed to Muhammad Abu Nasir ibn Yahya ibn Salam: the cancellation becomes effective when the month exits. This is supported by the idea that the cancellation can be aligned to a time when the right to cancel exists.
Intra-Hanafi disagreement.
3
Understand the rationale
The primary view defers cancellation because the act of cancellation during the month is not compatible with a monthly tenancy that inherently terminates at month's end. The right to cancel exists only at the start of a new rental period.
Based on the nature of monthly lease cycles.
4
Apply the principle of idafah (deferment)
If the canceling party explicitly states that the cancellation is effective from the beginning of the next month, it takes effect at that time without doubt. This is because lease contracts can be concluded with idafah, and cancellation, being the reverse of the contract, follows the same rule.
Idafah makes the cancellation operative at the future time.
5
Extract the thamarah (practical consequence)
Under the primary view, a mid-month cancellation means the tenancy continues until month-end; the tenant owes rent for the full month. Under the alternative view, the cancellation also becomes effective at month-end, so the practical result is the same. The difference lies in the reasoning, not the outcome.
Minimal practical difference between the two views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو فسخ في أثناء الشهر لم ينفسخ، وقيل: ينفسخ به إذا خرج الشهر؛ لأنه أمكن توفيقه إلى وقت يملك فيه الفسخ، وبه كان يفتي محمد أبو نصير بن يحيى بن سلام.
ولو قال: في أثناء الشهر فسخت رأس الشهر ينفسخ إذا أهل الشهر بلا شبهة، فيكون فسخاً مضافاً إلى رأس الشهر، وعقد الإجارة يصح مضافاً، فكذا فسخه. كذا في تبيين الحقائق للعلامة الزيلعي.
And if he cancels during the month, it does not become void, but it is said: it becomes void when the month exits, because it could be aligned to a time when he owns the cancellation, and this was the fatwa of Muhammad Abu Nasir ibn Yahya ibn Salam.
And if he says: I canceled in the middle of the month at the beginning of the month, it becomes void when the month appears without doubt, so it is a cancellation attached to the beginning of the month, and the lease contract is valid when attached, so likewise its cancellation. Thus in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq by al-Zaila'i.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of cancellation (faskh) announced in the middle of a month under a per-month rental contract. The main ruling is that if someone cancels during the month, the cancellation does not take immediate effect; the lease continues until the end of the month. However, there is a view that the cancellation becomes effective when the month exits, because the cancellation can be deferred to a time when he legally has the right to cancel (i.e., at the beginning of the next month). This view was followed by Muhammad Abu Nasir ibn Yahya ibn Salam in his fatwas. Additionally, if a person explicitly states that he cancels 'at the beginning of the month' while still in the middle of the month, the cancellation takes effect at the crescent of the next month without any doubt. This is because he has attached the cancellation to a future time, and since a lease contract can be validly concluded as a deferred contract, the cancellation can also be deferred. This ruling is cited from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq. The lesson demonstrates the Hanafi principle that cancellation of a lease is subject to the same rules as the contract itself regarding deferment.

Key Terms
فسخ (Faskh): Cancellation or termination of a lease contract by one party due to a right.
إضافة (Idafah): Attachment or deferment of a legal act to a future time.
شهر (Shahr): Month; in lease context, the rental period (usually from one month start to the next).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The lessor must agree.

Key Takeaway
Lease cancellation announced mid-month is deferred to the end of the month, reflecting the Hanafi principle of idafah in contract termination.

Leasing for a Year Without Specifying Monthly Rent
Ruling on yearly lease without monthly breakdown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a lease contract when monthly rent is not specified, and identify the starting point of the lease term.

Core Idea
A lease is valid if total duration and total rent are known, even without monthly breakdown.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi ijara law: a lease for a known period (e.g., one year) with a fixed total rent is valid even if the parties do not break down the rent into monthly installments. The passage also clarifies how to determine the start of the lease term when no starting date is specified. Understanding this ruling helps avoid unnecessary disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leasing a house for one year with a fixed total rent. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) despite not specifying the monthly rent installments.
The Hanafi school holds that knowledge of the total rent and duration suffices.
2
Locate the reasoning
The reasoning is that the duration is known, and the total rent is agreed, so it is analogous to a one-month lease which is valid even without daily breakdown.
The analogy highlights that as long as the overall term and price are certain, granular breakdown is not required.
3
Understand the equal division
Once valid, the total rent is divided equally among the months. Fluctuations in market prices during the lease term are not considered.
This prevents disputes over varying rental values.
4
Determine the start of the lease term
If a specific start month is mentioned (e.g., Ramadan), that is the start. If not, the lease begins at the time of the contract.
This is contrasted with a vow to fast, which does not automatically start the following month because fasting has specific times (daytime).
5
Apply the analogy and distinction
The lease start is like an oath of silence—immediate. But a vow to fast has restrictions that delay automatic start.
This illustrates the Hanafi method of qiyas and distinguishing causes.

وإجارتها سنةً بكذا وإن لم يسمّ قسط كلّ شهر، وأوّل المدة ما سمّي، وإلا فوقت العقد
[وشرح ذلك:] (قوله : وإجارتها...الخ؛ عطف على قوله : إجارة الدار؛ أي وصح إجارة الدارِ سنة بعشرة دراهم مثلاً، وإن لم يبين قسط كلّ شهر من الأجرة؛ لأنَّ المدة معلومة بدون التقسيم، فصار كإجارة شهر واحد، فإنّه جائز، وإن لم يبين قسط كل يوم فإذا صح وجب أن يقسم الأجر على الأشهر على السواء، ولا يعتبر تفاوت الأسعار باختلاف الزمان. [٢] قوله : وأوّل المدة ... الخ؛ يعني ابتداء مدَّةِ الإجارة ما سمى إن وقعت التسمية بأن يقول : من شهر رمضان من هذه السنة، وإن لم يقع التسمية فوقت العقد، هو المعتبر في ابتداء المدّة؛ لأنّ الأوقات كلّها متساوية بالنسبة إلى ذلك العقد. فإنّ كل الأوقاتِ محل للإجارة لعدم المنافاة بين الإجارة وبين وقت ما أصلاً، فتعين الزمانُ الذي يعقبه، كما إذا حلف لا يكلّمُ فلاناً شهراً، فيعتبر ابتداءه من يوم الحلف. بخلاف ما إذا نذر أن يصوم شهراً حيث لا يتعيّن الشهر الذي يلي النذر؛ لأنَّ الصوم يختص ببعض الأوقات، فإنَّ الليل ليس بمحل له، فلا يتعين ما يعقب سببه، وإن بين المدة تعين ذلك، وهو ظاهر.)
And leasing it for a year for such-and-such (amount) even if he does not specify the installment of each month, and the beginning of the term is what is specified, otherwise it is the time of the contract. (Explanation:) (His saying: 'And leasing it...' etc. is a conjunct to his saying: 'Leasing the house'; meaning: the leasing of the house for a year for ten dirhams, for example, is valid even if he does not specify the installment of each month from the rent, because the duration is known without division, so it becomes like leasing for one month, which is permissible even if he does not specify the installment of each day. So when it is valid, the rent must be divided equally over the months, and the variation of prices due to different times is not considered. [2] His saying: 'And the beginning of the term...' etc.; meaning: the start of the lease period is what is specified if specification occurs, such as saying: from Ramadan of this year, and if specification does not occur, then the time of the contract is what is considered as the beginning of the period; because all times are equal in relation to that contract. For all times are viable for leasing due to no incompatibility between leasing and any time at all, so the time that follows it is determined, just as if he swore he would not speak to so-and-so for a month, then the beginning is considered from the day of the oath. Unlike if he vows to fast a month, where the month following the vow is not determined; because fasting is specific to some times, as the night is not viable for it, so what follows its cause is not determined, and if he specifies the duration it is determined, and that is apparent.)
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the validity of a lease contract for a period of one year without specifying the rent for each month individually. The commentator explains that the contract is valid because the total duration is known, and the total rent is agreed upon, so it is like a one-month lease. Once valid, the total rent is divided equally among the months regardless of market fluctuations. The passage also discusses the start of the lease term: if the parties specify a starting month (e.g., Ramadan), that is the start; if not, the contract begins at the time of the contract. The commentator analogizes this to an oath of silence for a month, which begins from the moment of the oath. He contrasts it with a vow to fast, where the month is not automatically the next month because fasting has specific times (daytime). This is a typical Hanafi usul approach of distinguishing between different types of obligations.

Key Terms
قسط (qist): Installment or portion of rent allocated to a specific time period.
مدة (mudda): The duration or term of the lease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone leases a house for one year for 1200 dirhams without specifying the monthly rent, is the contract valid?
A) Yes, because the total duration and rent are known.
B) No, because monthly rent must be specified.
C) Yes, but only if the rent is paid upfront.
D) No, because the contract is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a lease is valid if the total duration and total rent are known; monthly breakdown is not necessary, and the lease term begins at the specified date or, if unspecified, at the time of the contract.
